Current Commentary

Reflections on Financial Austerity in Guizhou Province 27

— Ren

Recently, it was reported that Guizhou Province's income has decreased due to the implementation of the opium prohibition. The provincial government has decided to, starting from May 1st, abolish redundant agencies and suspend or reduce various subsidies. It is estimated that more than 23,000 yuan can be saved each month. This matter is a very fortunate piece of news in today's China, where financial management is needed.

For more than twenty years since the founding of the Republic of China, the finances, whether central or local, have generally been in deficit, with accumulated debts. Generally speaking, almost every province is in deficit, and debts are incurred every year. These deficits and debts are mostly caused by the expansion of government expenses. Since the establishment of the National Government, the administration of officials has been improved compared to the former Northern Government era. However, the phenomenon of establishing positions based on individuals seems not to have been completely eliminated. This is especially evident in the frontier provinces. In recent years, those who have discussed streamlining finances have mostly paid attention to this. Therefore, the saying of "increasing revenue and reducing expenditure" has gradually become the only way to manage finances.

Increasing revenue and reducing expenditure are two different things. To increase revenue, there must be a source to open up and open up, which must not harm the people. To reduce expenditure, there must be an outflow to reduce and reduce, which must not hinder governance. Judging from the current situation in our country, the national economy is declining, there are not many sources to open up, and government expenses are increasing daily. It seems that there are not a few outflows that can be reduced. In terms of the difficulty of financial reorganization, it may be easier to reduce expenditure than to increase revenue. Although, according to the principle, the national finances should be "expenditure based on income," the so-called "expenditure" must be the necessary "expenditure" related to the future of the country, and not include all unnecessary expenditures. As for today's Chinese financial expenditures, such as the expenses of redundant agencies, all are unnecessary expenditures.

The national finances are taken from the people and used for the people. Therefore, to ensure that there is no shortage of finances, we must take into account the people's ability to bear the burden while distributing funds. Then, the national administration will not be hindered as a result, and the national economy will not be damaged as a result. In other words, if one unnecessary expenditure can be saved today, it will preserve one more point of vitality for the people, and it will also increase one more source of revenue for future finances.

Today, Guizhou Province only saves more than 23,000 yuan per month. In terms of financial figures, the amount is extremely small. However, what is insufficient on a monthly basis is more than enough on an annual basis. Saving 23,000 yuan per month translates to saving 276,000 yuan per year. If this policy can be expanded and implemented in the eight provinces under the opium prohibition order, each province will save 270,000 yuan per year, then it will reach 2.2 million yuan in the blink of an eye. If all provinces in the country can hear the news and be motivated to implement it, then it would not be difficult to achieve an annual savings of 8 to 9 million yuan in local finances. If we go a step further and the central finances can also be appropriately tightened, then it may not be difficult to save tens of millions of yuan a year. Accumulating little by little can make a fur coat, and gathering sand can form an island. At this time of national and public hardship, if the national finances can all implement austerity like Guizhou Province, then not only can it create a new era for Chinese finances, but it can also be a way to improve the current national economic environment.

Correction: In the last line of yesterday's news commentary, "For the future of the European peace situation," the word "peace" was wrong.

I, the typesetter, hereby correct it.

Twenty-One American Nations Sign Multilateral Convention; Establish Special Flag to Protect Cultural Buildings in Wartime 28

(Washington) Today is Pan-American Day. Diplomatic representatives from twenty countries in the Americas (including Mexico, Guatemala, Honduras, El Salvador, Nicaragua, Costa Rica, and Panama from Central America; Cuba, Haiti, and Santo Domingo from the West Indies; and Venezuela, Colombia, Ecuador, Peru, Brazil, Bolivia, Chile, Argentina, Paraguay, and Uruguay from South America) gathered at the White House and signed a multilateral convention with the United States, stipulating that historical relics and artistic and cultural works of the American countries should be protected in wartime, and a special flag should be established. American Shipping Subsidy Bill; Roosevelt Holds Three Reasons 31

(Washington) President Roosevelt sent a letter to Congress on March 4, advocating the subsidy of American shipping, for three reasons: (1) The subsidies or other preferential measures obtained by the shipping industry of other countries in peacetime may put American merchants at a disadvantage; (2) If the United States is a neutral country in wartime and does not have sufficient merchant ships, it will not be able to engage in trade between neutral countries; (3) If the United States is a belligerent country in wartime, there will be a greater need for American ships, not only to be used as auxiliary naval vessels, but also to maintain considerable commerce. As for how much the subsidy will be, President Roosevelt did not specify, but wants to let Congress decide. Today, the Senate and House of Representatives, in accordance with President Roosevelt's wishes, have proposed a bill to directly subsidize American shipping in order to maintain a large number of merchant ships. (Reuters Dispatch, 15th)

Pacific Problem Investigation Conference Opens 32

(Tokyo) A special investigation conference on Pacific problems, gathering scholars from China, Japan, the United States, the Philippines, and the Dutch East Indies, focusing on the standard of living of the people, discussing international comparative methods, and discussing cultural issues such as land and population problems and immigration issues in all countries along the Pacific coast, will be held from the 16th to the 24th. The meetings will be held successively in the Osaka Building in Uchiyamashita-cho. The first meeting was held on the 16th, which opened at 9:30 a.m. on the same day. A total of 25 representatives from various countries attended, sitting around a table. First, Dr. Karl Olsberg, Professor of Stanford University in the United States and Chairman of the Pacific Problem Investigation Committee, delivered the opening address. Next, the chairman announced the agenda of the meeting. Then, the representatives presented the summary of the investigation reports they brought from their respective countries. From 10:30 a.m., the central topic of this meeting, namely the standard of living of the people, was discussed. At noon, the meeting was temporarily adjourned, and the discussion continued in the afternoon. (Nippon Union Dispatch, 16th)

Singapore Government Proposes Secret Protection Bill 33

(Tokyo) According to a telegram from the Japanese Consul in Singapore to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the 15th, the Singapore government submitted a draft secret protection bill to the Legislative Council, which opened on the 15th, and it has been officially announced in the gazette. The text of this bill is quite long, and its main points are based on the Secret Law enacted by the British Parliament in 1922, with changes or supplements added to suit the needs of the Straits Settlements region. It stipulates the rules for cracking down on illegal communication of secret agents, forgery of official documents, and intrusion into prohibited areas, as well as the public's reporting obligations for other crimes, etc. (Dentsu Agency Telegram, 16th)

France Directly Asks League of Nations Administrative Council to Condemn Germany's Military Conscription System; Extraordinary Means to Promote the Passage of the Motion, Poland and Other Countries Will Vote Against It 41

(Geneva) This afternoon, French Foreign Minister Laval, in the tense atmosphere of the League of Nations Administrative Council meeting, proposed a resolution in the name of the British, Italian, and French governments to denounce the German government for violating the military clauses of the Treaty of Versailles and reimplementing the forced military service policy, and stated that the League of Nations must reprimand the German government for this move and should find ways to make the League of Nations Covenant more effective in the collective security organization. The League of Nations Administrative Council must bear the responsibility of maintaining peace entrusted to it, and the Administrative Council cannot remain silent and stand idly by. The resolution firmly stated that Germany has no right to pass the forced military service law that conflicts with the Treaty of Versailles. (Reuters Dispatch, 16th)

(Geneva) The League of Nations Administrative Council was originally scheduled to meet this morning, but it has been changed to this afternoon to consider France's application against Germany's re-implementation of conscription. It is heard that the French representative, in view of the difficulty in appointing a rapporteur for the review, will directly submit a motion to the Administrative Council without going through the usual procedure of drafting a motion by the rapporteur. It is heard that this motion contains a paragraph condemning German policy. Poland, Denmark, and some South American countries will vote against this motion. However, the Administrative Council will be able to censure Germany's violation of the Treaty of Versailles by a majority. (Reuters Dispatch, 16th)

(Geneva) This afternoon, French Foreign Minister Laval will submit a motion to the League of Nations Administrative Council, the content of which is as follows:

(1) The Administrative Council expresses its opposition to the German government's policy of unilaterally abolishing the military clauses of the Treaty of Versailles decided on March 16.

(2) Invite the member states of the League of Nations to establish various new agreements to improve the European security system.

(3) The Administrative Council shall appoint a subcommittee to study the economic and financial sanctions that should be taken against countries that violate treaties, even if the countries that violate treaties are not engaged in war, these sanctions may also be imposed. In other words, the provisions of Article 16 of the League of Nations Covenant will be extended. After Laval submits the above motion, he will probably urge the Administrative Council to make a decision immediately, and even advocate that it should be submitted for expression without going through the rapporteur's review. According to the procedure previously set by the Administrative Council, the proposal must first be submitted to the rapporteur for review, and then a report is submitted to the Administrative Council, and then it is submitted for a vote. It is now heard that some delegations are unwilling to participate in the section on morally opposing Germany's attitude, so France believes that it is more appropriate to change the planned procedure and submit the entire issue of respecting treaties to the Administrative Council for a vote. According to Havas Agency's exploration, Britain and Italy will do their best to support France's request. The diplomatic circles heard that France's decision was quite sensational for a while. When this motion is submitted for a vote in the Administrative Council, it can be expected to pass unanimously, except for some countries that abstain from voting. (Havas Dispatch, 16th)

(Geneva) According to information from the French representative here, the League of Nations Administrative Council will appoint a three-person committee at today's meeting to study the issue of protesting Germany's restoration of conscription in the French memorandum. These three people are probably the Spanish representative Madariaga, the Danish Foreign Minister Mengqi, and the Chilean representative Vicuna. (National Telegram, 16th)

League of Nations Administrative Council First Does Preparatory Work; French Newspapers Believe that the Meeting Situation Is Still Satisfactory 42

(Geneva) When the League of Nations Administrative Council held a closed-door meeting yesterday, it discussed the border dispute between Italy and Albania. After a brief discussion, it was decided to consider it at the meeting in May. Today, the Administrative Council will hold a closed-door meeting to elect a rapporteur for France's complaint against Germany's re-implementation of forced military service. After the rapporteur is elected, the first public meeting will be held. At that time, French Foreign Minister Laval will submit the French memorandum, and then prominent politicians such as British Foreign Secretary Simon will speak in succession. (Reuters Dispatch, 16th)

(Paris) The extraordinary meeting of the League of Nations Administrative Council was held for the first time yesterday, and it could only do preparatory work. The newspapers did not think it was unusual, and they believed that the three countries, Britain, France, and Italy, completely agreed on the resolution that the Administrative Council should pass, but there were some differences in form. Morning Post said: Although Poland's attitude is hesitant, the Administrative Council's "meeting situation yesterday was still satisfactory. Britain, France, and Italy have established a close compromise, and the Czech Republic will also join." Business Report said: "The general opinion in Geneva is that if the French delegation insists on its position, the wording of the communiqué issued by the Stresa Conference will definitely be maintained to the end. The results of the Stresa Conference are even more valuable than the verbal accusations of Germany by the League of Nations Administrative Council." The Paris Echo said that although the League of Nations Administrative Council will eventually condemn Germany, it will have to spend some effort. Several newspapers believe that since Germany's reorganization of its military has been submitted to the League of Nations for trial, it will definitely be judged fairly without being vague. For example, Exiles News said: "If the League of Nations Administrative Council adopts a resolution with moderate wording to end Germany's breach of contract, this is completely contrary to the original purpose of the Administrative Council's convening. In short, no one expects sanctions. Since the Administrative Council does not take sanctions, it can only verbally accuse Germany in spirit." The Little Parisian said: "The principles of justice and morality, as well as thousands of years of civilized customs, cannot be treated as child's play." The Little Daily said: "Judging from the current negotiations, the Administrative Council will not be able to end its work until Friday evening, but it is hoped that it will achieve practical results. "The Administrative Council will end the discussion in a way that does not involve ambiguity. Its wording is very clear and must be firm. This is beyond doubt." (Havas Agency Telegram, 16th)

If Germany Destroys the Rhineland, Britain and Italy Will Provide Substantial Assistance to France; Northern European Countries Advocate a Moderate Approach to Germany 43

(Geneva) The League of Nations Administrative Council met today to discuss the issue of France's request to condemn Germany for violating the Treaty of Versailles. It is learned that if Germany violates the treaty in the demilitarized zone on its border, Britain and Italy are prepared to provide France with military assistance. The two countries reiterated the promise of the Locarno Treaty at the Stresa Conference, guaranteeing peace in the Rhine area, and decided to take military action under certain conditions. The League of Nations Administrative Council's secret discussion lasted only one hour. After the adjournment, it was learned that the Scandinavian countries advocated a moderate approach to Germany and slightly reduced the intensity of the resolution proposed by France. Norwegian Foreign Minister Mengqi met with British Foreign Secretary Simon for a long time. After that, Mengqi urged the Administrative Council to pass a vague resolution and not condemn Germany for violating the treaty. At the same time, it was also learned that the British representative was very concerned that the cooperation between Britain and Italy in the Stresa Declaration might be misunderstood by Berlin as a threat to the German government. Therefore, the British representative made a cautious statement tonight in order to dispel the misunderstanding, saying that this declaration "is not a promise of assistance to France, but a mutual agreement." The French side is doing its best to take strict action against Germany. The French representative has contacted Denmark, Poland, and other countries that want to maintain good relations with Germany and advocate a moderate approach, intending to make them not object and pass the resolution of the Stresa Three-Power Conference. As for Soviet Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov, he still felt that the resolution was too moderate. However, after Litvinov learned that French Foreign Minister Laval had consulted with the representatives of the Little Entente and obtained their support, he also withdrew his opposition. According to reliable sources, the Little Entente has allowed Austria, Hungary, and Bulgaria to each have an army of 75,000 men. Czech Foreign Minister Benes told Laval that the Little Entente does not object to the three countries increasing their self-defense forces, but it must be guaranteed that the three countries can participate in the security pact. The attitude of the Little Entente can be summarized in the words of a certain spokesperson, who said, "We are quite satisfied with the results of the Stresa Conference. Now we only pay attention to future issues. The most important thing is the covenant to maintain Austria's independence." The Administrative Council will meet again tomorrow. Sources expect that the League of Nations will pass a declaration, the main points of which are as follows:

(1) The League of Nations cannot regard Germany's abolition of the Treaty of Versailles as legal.

(2) Germany's actions are "regrettable," because this move is an attack on all treaties.

(3) Since Germany has violated the treaty, it is necessary to study in detail how to deal with future violations. The British side here admits that the joint declaration of Stresa does contain the meaning of Britain's guarantee to maintain Germany's demilitarized zone on the border, but it claims that this declaration is not specifically aimed at Germany. The British spokesman also said that the declaration not only protects France from Germany's aggression, but also protects Germany from France's aggression. (National Telegram, 16th)

(London) According to the British Parliament, the representatives of Britain who attended the Stresa Conference did not accept any new restrictions on the European continent. This is very satisfactory. The Parliament also believes that Germany's acceptance of negotiations on a general non-aggression pact does not prevent other countries from concluding bilateral mutual assistance pacts. This move is a real progress in the international situation. However, one cannot expect too much practical effect from Germany's new attitude. As for the reorganization of the military in Austria, Hungary, and Bulgaria, it is said that it is not impossible to grant Austria, Hungary, and Bulgaria the right to military equality, but it is hoped that this equality will not exceed a certain reasonable limit. (Havas Dispatch, 15th)

British New Budget; Total Expenditure of 750 Million Pounds; Increased and Decreased Tax Rates; Expanding Defense Spending 50

(London) Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain presented the 1935-36 budget to the House of Commons this afternoon. The total expenditure is estimated at £729,970,000, including £235,580,000 for repayment of principal and interest on public debt, £490,390,000 for various government expenses, and the remainder for temporary expenditures. The defense expenditure for the army, navy, and air force in this budget is £10.05 million more than the previous budget. The total revenue, estimated according to the current tax rules, is £735,580,000, which, after deducting expenditures, leaves a surplus of £5,610,000. (Havas dispatch, 15th)

(London) Although Chancellor Chamberlain's fourth budget, presented to the House of Commons this afternoon, indicated the stability of British finances and a gradual restoration of world confidence, it did not cause excitement in London. However, bankers were comforted by the fact that the pound sterling was heavily attacked last year, but the equalization fund was still profitable. The stock exchange took the budget calmly because it was as expected. It is widely believed that the restoration of government employees' salaries and the increase in allowances will enhance the current government's support among voters. The important changes to the tax rates in the budget are: income tax on the first £135 is reduced from 27 pence per pound to 18 pence per pound; the threshold for married individuals is raised from £150 to £170; and in view of the decrease in the birth rate, the allowance for children after the first child is increased from £40 to £50. The tax exemption for single individuals is limited to £125. The reduction in official salaries in 1931 will be fully restored from July 1, costing an additional £4 million. Unmilled rice will be taxed at two-thirds of a penny per pound, and soybeans will be taxed at 10% ad valorem. The free preferential tariff for soybeans will be implemented from August 1. Entertainment tax for seats costing 6 pence or less will be abolished. When presenting the bill, Chamberlain said that, generally speaking, we can say that we have restored 80% of prosperity. Our job today is to restore the remaining 20% without damaging the credit that has already been built. If there is peace abroad and unity at home, there is no reason to say that we should not make great progress towards prosperity this year. The budget estimate is made with this belief. Chamberlain also mentioned the achievements of last year, saying that industrial production increased by about 12%, manufacturing production has set a new record, exports have increased by £30 million, interest rates remain low, and the number of major projects has increased greatly, especially in construction. The cost of living for the whole year is still much lower than in 1931, retail sales continue to develop, and national savings are no less than before. The net increase in the Post Office Savings Bank, Trustee Savings Bank, and sales of savings certificates is about £50 million. This continuous progress has now been realized. This is no longer a question. The results are so good that there is nothing like it in the world. It is estimated that expenditure next year will be £730 million. Revenue, estimated on the basis of current taxes, can reach £736.6 million, leaving a surplus of £5.6 million. (Reuters dispatch, 15th)

(London) Those who benefit from the restoration of salaries and the reduction of entertainment tax and income tax have praised this budget, while the increase in heavy oil and soybean taxes and the reduction in road maintenance funds have been criticized by those involved in road transport, animal husbandry, and the automobile industry. Chancellor Chamberlain delivered a radio address from London last night, calling this a budget for the poor, but public opinion seems to refer to this as a budget for the lower middle class. The *Daily Express* said that this budget aims to win the favor of the two million income taxpayers, while the 17 million working families will gain nothing except for slightly cheaper movie tickets. This view is not entirely agreed upon. According to *The Times*, the government is still confident that a general election will not be held before 1936. Generally speaking, the newspapers welcome this budget, but the reduction of road maintenance funds and the lack of provisions for debt repayment reserves have been criticized by some newspapers. (Reuters dispatch, 16th)

(London) The House of Commons is scheduled to adjourn for four days for Easter and will reconvene on April 29. (Reuters dispatch, 16th)

Germany Promotes "Recreational Fitness" Movement; Weekend Outings Beneficial for Physical and Mental Health and Crucial for Increasing National Strength 51

(Berlin) Recently, a "Recreational Fitness" movement has been reorganized in Germany and is being promoted nationwide, aiming to encourage all working people to participate in this exercise. The association recently issued a declaration stating that, out of Germany's 30 million adults, only 7 million actually participate in various games and sports. The remaining 23 million are working people who lack exercise. However, these hardworking people, especially the elderly, although they know that their physical strength is declining and they can no longer compete with young people, must feel the urgent need for appropriate relaxation exercises. If they can temporarily leave the city every weekend to relax their body and mind in the city parks, it will be of great benefit to their physical health. Walking and swimming are especially important for restoring health. If everyone can follow this, not only will individuals benefit infinitely, but it will also be crucial for increasing national strength. Therefore, the association has decided to expand its promotion, hoping to awaken all working people across the country, so that they can understand the benefits of exercise and make weekend outings a common and good habit. (National Telegraph, 15th)

International Commercial Telegram - Reuters Special Business Report, April 16th - 95

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: Today, 143 shillings and 4 pence, down 7 pence.

London Silver Bullion: The silver market was loose today. The spot price is 30 pence 1.9375, and the futures price is 31 pence 0.0625, both down 3.125. China bought and resold, and India sold.

Bombay Silver Bullion: The silver market was weak today. The spot price is 72 rupees and 5 annas, down 17 annas.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The London foreign exchange market was quiet today, with minor transactions. The British-American exchange rate opened at $4.85625, 375 higher than yesterday's closing rate. It trended lower in the morning, but at 2 PM, the price was $4.86, 375 higher than the opening rate.

British-French: The opening price rose by 8 points, at 73 francs 59. Later, it became stronger, but at 1 PM, it dropped from 73 francs 71 to 73 francs 69, which was still 10 points higher than the opening price. This price remained unchanged until the time of the telegram.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The New York cotton market opened lower due to bad news. It is reported that the cotton textile industry plans to sue the government in court over the continued donation issue. The government's new cotton production program has not yet been determined, so speculators are waiting and seeing, but some industry players are buying.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market was looser today. At 1 PM, the July futures price fell by 4 points to 6.36.

Indian Cotton: The Bombay cotton market was flat today as bulls closed out positions and European exporters sold. The price of July/August Broach cotton was 230 rupees 75, down 5 rupees.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market continued to be loose. At 1 PM, the July futures price was 5 shillings 8.125 pence.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market fell first and then rose. The price fell at the opening, and then recovered, because there are serious reports of damage to 12 million acres of wheat fields in North and South Dakota, Nebraska, Kansas, and Oklahoma.

Rubber

London: The rubber market was more active today. The transaction price for July/September at noon was 5.875 pence, 0.125 lower than yesterday's closing price.

New York: The rubber market was looser today, due to the low price in London. The buying interest is weak, and the market is quiet.

New York: The securities market opened quietly this morning, with little price fluctuation. It is expected that railway stocks will continue to rebound. The New York securities market prices are listed on the left.
