Li Guojie's Appeal Case - High Court Verdict 96

Suzhou News: After Li Guojie of China Merchants Bureau appealed to the Jiangsu High Court, the High Court repeatedly sent personnel to Shanghai to conduct trials in the Shanghai Local Court. The court proceedings and the altered conviction were reported in previous newspapers. Now the full text of the verdict in this case has been finalized by the High Court and printed yesterday (16th) afternoon. A true copy is recorded as follows:

Jiangsu High Court Criminal Verdict, 21st Year (23rd Year Conclusion), Suit No. 1060. Appellant: Li Guojie, male, 55 years old, native of Hefei County, Anhui Province, residing on Henry Road, Shanghai, former General Manager of China Merchants Bureau. Defense Attorneys: Lawyer Lu Hongyi, Lawyer Lu Shifang, Lawyer Jiang Yiping. The above-mentioned appellant, in the case of breach of duty, being dissatisfied with the first-instance judgment of the Shanghai Local Court on December 27, 21st year of the Republic of China, filed an appeal. After the judgment of this court, he appealed to the Supreme Court, which remanded the case to this court for retrial as follows:

Main Text: The original judgment regarding the crime and sentence of breach of duty is revoked. Li Guojie, with the intention of illegal possession for himself, embezzled public property in his possession and is sentenced to imprisonment for one year and two months. The number of days of detention before the final judgment is determined to be offset against the term of imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day.

Facts: Li Guojie was originally the Chairman of the Board of Directors of the Shanghai China Merchants Bureau. On February 26, 21st year of the Republic of China, he was also appointed by the Ministry of Communications as the General Manager of the Bureau. At the same time, Chen Fumu, the Vice Minister of Communications, was appointed to serve concurrently as the Supervisor of the Bureau. After Li Guojie took office, he believed that the poor performance of the China Merchants Bureau over the years was due to the dilapidated ships, incomplete docks, and cargo handling facilities. Unless a large sum of money was borrowed to pay off old debts, redeem mortgaged properties, add ships, and build docks and warehouses, there would be no other way to reorganize. He then submitted a report to Supervisor Chen Fumu for approval to mortgage the land and buildings along the Bund and Sichuan Road on Fuzhou Road, Shanghai, and the Zhongbei Hua and other warehouses and docks, to the Shanghai China General Corporation for Shanghai taels of silver each, with an agreement to receive 85% in actual value, a commission of 2%, and an annual interest rate of 9%, for a period of 20 years, and two contracts were signed, referred to as the "Construction Loan" and the "Dock Loan". Another memorandum for the purchase of ships on credit was signed, referred to as the "Ship Purchase Loan," which was to order 30 new-style ships from the American Da Lai Shipping Company for the China Merchants Bureau to use. The ship prices were negotiated according to the market value at the time and were all treated as loans, with a corresponding interest rate. On September 5th and 6th, Li Guojie and China General Corporation signed the aforementioned contracts separately and submitted them to Supervisor Chen Fumu for stamping. Unexpectedly, Chen Fumu took the opportunity to demand bribes from Li Guojie, intentionally withholding the contracts. Li Guojie, because China General Corporation repeatedly urged him, fearing that the plan would fail, on the 23rd of the same month, negotiated with China General Corporation to advance 700,000 taels of silver from the 20 million tael loan and disposed of it without authorization, handing it over to Huang Jusu, a representative sent by Chen Fumu, for Chen Fumu to receive, intending to gradually make up for it in the future when business developed. Therefore, he did not record it in the China Merchants Bureau's accounts. At the same time, after Chen Fumu received the money, he returned the contracts. Not long after, Chen Fumu left his post. Li Guojie, because he could not make up for the 700,000 taels he had advanced, intending to escape his own involvement, wrote a letter to the Minister of Communications reporting Chen Fumu's extortion. The Ministry of Communications then ordered the Shanghai Municipal Government to arrest Li Guojie in November of the same year and send him to the Shanghai Local Court Prosecutor for investigation and prosecution.

Reasons: After the appellant in this case took office as the General Manager of the China Merchants Bureau, he submitted a report to Supervisor Chen Fumu for approval and signed construction loan and dock loan contracts with the American China General Corporation, mortgaging the land and buildings along the Bund and Sichuan Road on Fuzhou Road, Shanghai, and the Zhongbei Hua and other warehouses and docks, for a total of Shanghai taels of silver each. In addition, a ship purchase loan contract was signed. On September 5th and 6th, 21st year of the Republic of China, it was signed with China General Corporation separately. Then, on the 23rd of the same month, 700,000 taels were advanced from the 20 million tael loan and handed over to Huang Jusu, Chen Fumu's representative, for Chen Fumu to receive. Not only has the appellant repeatedly stated this in court, but also the China General Corporation delivered ten promissory notes from the McCalie Bank and one promissory note from the HSBC Bank, each worth 50,000 taels of silver, to the appellant on September 23, 21st year of the Republic of China, plus one promissory note from HSBC Bank and one promissory note from Citibank, each worth 71,736 yuan and 01 cents, calculated at 0.0697 taels per yuan, each equivalent to 50,000 taels of silver, totaling 700,000 taels, which have also been investigated and verified by the Prosecutor of the original court and this court. After Chen Fumu received them, he and Huang Jusu used pseudonyms such as Chen Shaode, Chen Zesheng, Wei Junhong, Wei Zhenhong, Huang Weiruo, Huang Zhongde, Huang Zhengde, Huang Yude, Feng Duanyi, Feng Shuyan, etc., and deposited them in the Zhongfu, Jin Cheng, China banks and the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau on the 24th, 26th, 27th, and 29th of the same month. There are bank statements available for verification. The addresses of the depositors, such as No. 28 Meili Garden, Da Xi Road, is Chen Fumu's residence, and No. 5 Zhaofeng Road is Huang's residence, which have also been proven by the door-keeper and the watchman Yao Dekui Hu Shuyou etc. Therefore, the appellant's claim that the 700,000 taels in advance were handed over to Chen Fumu is true. As for the reason for the delivery, the appellant argued that according to Articles 5, 2, 3, and 10 of the China Merchants Bureau Supervision Office Regulations, the formulation of contracts, the reorganization of capital, and other important matters all fell within the authority of the Supervision Office. The 700,000 taels in advance were part of the agreed loan and were specifically used for the reorganization of the China Merchants Bureau. Their receipt, storage, and management were naturally within the reorganization plan, and the matter was extremely important and naturally fell within the scope of the Supervision Office's authority. Chen Fumu had the right to receive and keep the money, and the appellant followed the order to withdraw and submit it. How can there be any embezzlement or bribery, etc. However, Article 1 of the China Merchants Bureau Supervision Office Regulations clearly stipulates that the China Merchants Bureau Supervision Office is solely responsible for supervision, and all reorganization plans of the Supervision Office should be the responsibility of the General Manager's Office for execution, as stipulated in Article 3 of the same Regulations and Article 2 of the China Merchants Bureau General Manager's Office Regulations. The Supervision Office is solely responsible for supervision, while the General Manager's Office is responsible for executing affairs. The authority is very clear. Moreover, the functions of the Supervision Office have been listed one by one in Article 5 of the Supervision Office Regulations, and there is no clear stipulation for receiving, paying, and keeping money. However, Articles 10, 1, and 2 of the General Manager's Office Regulations clearly state the functions of the Accounting Department of the General Manager's Office, including "receipt and payment of cash" and "safekeeping of bank books and checks." Although the 700,000 taels in advance were generated from the signing of the contract, signing the contract is one matter, and receiving, paying, and keeping the money is another. Since they are separately stipulated in the regulations of the Supervision Office and the General Manager's Office, the result of signing the contract cannot be that all matters arising from the result of signing the contract are handled by the Supervision Office itself. The so-called other important matters refer to those not stipulated in the regulations. Receiving, paying, and keeping money have been clearly stipulated in Article 10 of the General Manager's Office Regulations and are not included in this general scope. The appellant also argued that Article 11 of the Supervision Office Regulations also stipulates that the Supervision Office may hire consultants to handle legal, accounting, and construction matters, but this refers to supervising accounting administration and not performing accounting duties. In short, the supervisory authority has no jurisdiction over all matters of the subordinate agency. To replace the subordinate agency to handle all affairs is not possible. Moreover, the China Merchants Bureau and China General Corporation agreed on the construction loan, dock loan, and ship purchase loan contracts, all of which must be stamped by the Supervisor, while the receipt of 700,000 taels in advance from China General Corporation was only issued by the General Manager. It can be seen that the appellant had long recognized the authority in signing the contract and receiving the money, and would never mistakenly believe that Chen Fumu had the authority to keep the money and rashly hand over 700,000 taels, which can be asserted. Even from the perspective of the delivery situation at the time, if Chen Fumu had indeed kept the 700,000 taels, why was there no clear order from the Supervision Office to withdraw the money? Why did the appellant not use an official document to present it when handing over the 700,000 taels? There was no formal receipt and no temporary receipt from the responsible person, and the China Merchants Bureau did not record it in any accounts. Even if it is believed that the money was specifically used for the reorganization of the China Merchants Bureau, separate books could have been created and specially recorded. How could the receipt of 700,000 taels be unaccountable? The saying of handing over for safekeeping is clearly an excuse to shirk responsibility afterwards and is difficult to believe. Furthermore, the appellant submitted a letter to the Minister of Communications on November 13, 21st year of the Republic of China, in which it was stated that the money was demanded by Supervisor Chen Fumu and that if it was not paid, the contract could not be established. Guojie dared to swear to heaven that he did not take a penny. Later, during the investigation by the original court, he still stated that after the borrowing contracts were signed, he used official documents to ask the Supervision Office to seal it. He then held the contract and refused to release it. At the same time, he asked people to express that he wanted to raise some funds and asked him what it would be used for. He refused to say. The price-maker did not know this situation and urged the contract. I had no choice but to ask the company to advance a batch of money first. Later, I paid the money on one side, and he delivered the contract on the other side. The 700,000 tael check was issued by the company. He demanded that it not be registered. I was really afraid that the China Merchants Bureau would close down, so I gave Chen Fumu 700,000 taels. I also intended to achieve great things without worrying about small expenses. As for this money, I thought that after the business got better in the future, I would gradually pay it back. It has been said that Chen Fumu requested bribery and the various circumstances of the delivery have been confessed. It is not an empty word. Taken together, when the appellant submitted the contracts for signing to the supervisor, Chen Fumu deliberately withheld the contract and took the opportunity to solicit bribes. The appellant then negotiated with China General Corporation to advance 700,000 taels of silver and hand it over to Chen Fumu, but did not record it in the China Merchants Bureau's accounts, preparing to gradually make up for it in the future when business developed. The appellant knew that the money belonged to the China Merchants Bureau and was specifically used for reorganization, but he exceeded his authority and disposed of it without authorization, transferring it to bribery funds, which shows that when he received the money, he had already regarded it as his own, so he dared to use it freely. Examining his actions, in addition to constituting the crime of delivering bribes, he should also be found guilty of embezzling public property in his possession. However, the reason for his embezzlement was due to bribery, which clearly has a method and result relationship. According to Article 74 of the Criminal Code, he should be sentenced to the more serious crime of embezzling public property. The original judgment recognized the crime of breach of trust under Article 366, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Code, which has been revoked by this court, and acquittal has been pronounced. Regarding the embezzlement part, since it was the result of delivering bribes, the original judgment did not discuss the bribery part. Chen Fumu was the supervisor of the China Merchants Bureau and signing contracts was his duty. When the appellant asked for the seal to be stamped, Chen Fumu took the opportunity to ask for bribes and was given them. Only the act of paying bribes to public officials regarding their duties should constitute a crime under Article 128, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Code. The original judgment erroneously believed that bribes were paid to public officials regarding acts in violation of their duties and should be charged with the crime under Article 129, Paragraph 3 of the Criminal Code, and also cited Paragraph 4 of the same article, ruling that 700,000 taels should be confiscated, and if they had disappeared, they should be recovered, without paying attention to the provisions of the second part of Article 62, Paragraph 1 of the same law, which were all incorrect. As for the appellant's report to the Minister of Communications, it was nothing more than an attempt to escape his own involvement, which did not meet the requirements of self-surrender stipulated in Article 38 of the Criminal Code. The original judgment's reference to that article to reduce the penalty by one-half was also not legal. Although the appeal in this case is groundless, the original judgment is also inappropriate and should still be revoked and revised by this court. In conclusion, in accordance with Article 385, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Procedure Law, Articles 357, Paragraph 1, 128, Paragraph 2, 74, and 64 of the Criminal Code, the judgment is as stated in the main text. Prosecutor Zhan Yuafen of this court executed the duties of the prosecutor at the court. The appellate court in this case is the Supreme Court. If the parties are dissatisfied with this judgment, they should file an appeal with this court within ten days from the day following the service of the judgment, with a written statement of the reasons for disagreement. April 5, 24th year of the Republic of China, Hu Shancheng, Presiding Judge of the Second Criminal Division of the Jiangsu High Court [Seal], Judge Zhang Bingci [Seal], Judge Zhang Zepu [Seal]. This is a true copy that is identical to the original. Clerk Ding Yi of the Jiangsu High Court, [Date].

Jiangsu High Court Criminal Verdict, 21st Year (23rd Year Conclusion), Suit No. (Supplementary 2) 1060. Plaintiff: China Merchants Bureau, Legal Representative Liu Hongsheng, male, 48 years old, native of Dinghai County, Zhejiang Province, residing at No. 2 Fuzhou Road, Shanghai, General Manager of China Merchants Bureau, Litigation Attorney Lawyer Wang Youling. Defendant: Li Guojie, male, 55 years old, native of Hefei County, Anhui Province, residing on Henry Road, Shanghai, former General Manager of China Merchants Bureau, Litigation Attorney Lawyer Lu Hongyi, Lawyer Lv Shifang, Lawyer Jiang Yiping. In the case of the above-mentioned plaintiff and defendant's appeal case, which is being tried in this court, a civil lawsuit is filed incidentally. This court's judgment is as follows:

Main Text: Li Guojie shall compensate the China Merchants Bureau 700,000 Shanghai taels of silver and pay interest at a rate of 8% per annum from April 28, 22nd year of the Republic of China until the date of settlement.

Facts: The plaintiff's attorney stated that the request was the judgment in the main text. His statement in essence stated that when the defendant was the General Manager of China Merchants Bureau, he signed a loan contract with China General Corporation. The corporation advanced 700,000 Shanghai taels of silver, which the defendant issued a receipt for and then disposed of himself while in possession, using it to pay bribes. The defendant should be held responsible for compensation. The Supreme Court remanded the case for further review on the public prosecution aspect, and the accompanying civil lawsuit was remanded along with it. If the public prosecution results in no changes, the attached civil lawsuit remains subject to the judgment prior to the further review. The defendant stated that the request should be to dismiss the plaintiff's lawsuit, arguing that I handed over the 700,000 taels to the supervisor, Chen Fumu. Chen Fumu should be held responsible and I cannot compensate on behalf of Chen Fumu.

Reasons: The facts determined by the criminal judgment, limited to the proof and liability related to the crime, have a binding effect on the accompanying civil lawsuit. This is clearly stated in Article 512 of the Criminal Procedure Law. In the present case, regarding the part of the public prosecution, this court has determined that after the defendant took office as the General Manager of the China Merchants Bureau, Chen Fumu, the supervisor, approved the signing of a 20 million tael loan contract with China General Corporation. When presenting the contract for approval, Chen Fumu took the opportunity to solicit bribes. The defendant then negotiated with the corporation to advance 700,000 Shanghai taels of silver and hand it over to Chen Fumu. It was determined that he was guilty of the crime of delivering bribes and embezzling public property for his duties. Based on Articles 357, Paragraph 1, 128, Paragraph 2, and 74 of the Criminal Code, a criminal sentence was ruled. Therefore, the defendant should bear the responsibility for compensating for the damage to the rights of others as a result of the crime. The plaintiff's attorney's request remains according to the original claim, the judgment on the defendant shall be to compensate 700,000 Shanghai taels of silver, and the interest is 8% per annum from April 28, 22nd year of the Republic of China, until the date of settlement, there is no objection, The defendant's excuse that the 700,000 taels were taken away by Chen Fumu and that Chen Fumu should be held responsible is not well-founded and should be rejected. Therefore, the defendant should be ordered to pay back to the plaintiff 700,000 silver dollars, calculated at 0.0715 taels per dollar, equivalent to 977,020.0979 yuan in silver dollars, and interest at a rate of 8% per annum from April 28, 22nd year of the Republic of China, until the date of settlement. Based on the above discussion, in accordance with Articles 509 and 507 of the Criminal Procedure Law and Article 184, Paragraph 1 of the Civil Code, the judgment is as stated in the main text. April 5, 24th year of the Republic of China, Hu Shancheng, Presiding Judge of the Second Criminal Division of the Jiangsu High Court, Judge Zhang Bingci, Judge Zhang Zepu. This is a true copy that is identical to the original. Clerk Ding Yi of the Jiangsu High Court, [Date].

Chinese Ratepayers Association of the International Settlement Held its Representative Assembly Yesterday and Elected Yu Qiaqing, Xu Xinliu and Five Others as Chinese Directors, Wang Yansong and Others as Committee Members, and Wang Boyuan as Land Committee Member; Resolved to Oppose Telephone Price Increases and Officially Issue a Declaration 97

The Chinese Ratepayers Association of the Public Concession held its first representative assembly yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM at the Bankers' Club on Hong Kong Road, where they elected directors and committee members to the Municipal Council, as well as the executive committee for this year. Yu Qiaqing, Wang Yansong, Wang Xiaolai, and others were elected. They also decided to issue a declaration the same day to oppose telephone price increases. Details of each are recorded below:

Representatives Present Yesterday's attendees included Zhao Tiezhang from the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Geng Jiaji from the Municipal Government, and 75 individuals including Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Wu Zhihao, Cao Zhigong, Gu Wensheng, Wang Honghui, Xu Jutang, Xu Wenzhao, Jin Runxiang, Hu Fengxiang, Yan Guangdi, Shen Tianxin, Chen Binghui, Xu Xiaochu, Chu Huiseng, Ma Shaoquan, Lu Wenshao, Mao Heyuan, Song Shixiang, Cheng Xiechun, and Xu Jiyu.

Assembly Staff Chairman: Wang Xiaolai; Vice Chairman: Xu Jiyu; Secretaries: Yan Kuasheng, Tao Ledong; Administrators: Gao Wosheng, Xu Fansun; Tellers for the Election of Chinese Directors: Cheng Xiechun, Qian Longzhang; Ballot Counters: Shen Tianxin, Yu Zhongxian; Tellers for the Chinese Committee: Chu Huiseng, Wang Yansong; Ballot Counters: Cao Zhigong, Ke Ganchen; Tellers for the Land Committee: Song Shixiang, Xie Zhongfu; Ballot Counters: Mao Heyuan, Zhang Henghai; Executives in Charge of Committee Reports: Wang Hanliang, Hu Fengxiang, Ye Jiaxing, Ma Shaoquan; Ballot Counters: Sun Mingqi, Wang Honghui, Chen Binghui, Zhang Yichen.

Chairman's Address The chairman of the representative assembly said in his speech: "Representatives from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, representatives from the Municipal Government, and fellow representatives, at a time when Shanghai is facing considerable difficulties, the responsibility of this Association is even greater than before. This is because the interests represented by this Association are not merely limited to the taxpayers of the Public Concession, but the interests and influence it can involve extend to the entire city, the entire country, and even the world. Therefore, the words and actions of this Association must not exceed the provisions of Article 2 of this Association's charter, which is to 'develop the autonomy of the concession and seek public interests and equal treatment.' The meaning and steps of this provision are that we must first develop autonomy before we can seek public interests and equal treatment. However, how to seek the development of autonomy, what methods and means to use, this requires political scholars to design. But reading the Tianjin Ta Kung Pao of March 16th, an article published by a German economic expert who is a consultant to the Economic Committee, it said, 'Some say that the Chinese people have not yet developed a degree of self-government. I believe that this argument is untenable, because the degree of local self-government is being gradually implemented in practice, so that there can be practical training before maturity can be spoken of. A great Prussian politician a hundred years ago, based on this view, coupled with a determination to carry it out, endowed the people who had not yet developed at all with a system of self-government, and achieved astonishing results. Therefore, I should also trust that the intelligent and virtuous Chinese people have the ability to self-govern.' In the chairman's speech at the first meeting of the previous representative assembly, in order to make the status of the Shanghai Special Zone particularly clear to Chinese and foreign people, it was said that once Chinese directors join the special zone's municipal administration, it becomes jointly managed by Chinese and foreigners. Therefore, in fact, the autonomous organ of the special zone has become a 'self-governing organ jointly run by Chinese and foreign residents.' If we can evolve from this, and give it a short period of time, it is definitely the most peaceful and straightforward way to unify and complete the administration of Shanghai." Therefore, anyone who recognizes this fact and understands the opinions of the above-mentioned German expert will enthusiastically support and encourage the vigorous progress of this Association based on its charter, which is something to be extremely fortunate about. However, the history of this Association, starting from October 14th of the Republic of China year 14, will soon be fifteen years. The Municipal Council of the Public Concession has had our local directors and committee members for seven terms. Whether we have the ability to operate and govern ourselves is not something that this Association can know on its own. However, since it is a self-government jointly run by Chinese and foreigners, the selection of people who represent us at the Municipal Council is naturally a matter of concern to foreigners. As far as can be recorded, (1) A year ago, during a debate in the British House of Lords on the China issue, Lord Eddington mentioned the Shanghai issue, saying that the Municipal Council now has five Chinese directors and countless Chinese committee members, whose work is very valuable. (2) The Feetham Report, and (3) the speech of the Chairman of the Annual Meeting of Taxpayers of the Municipal Council, all deeply praised the representatives of the taxpayers present at the Municipal Council, and considered the selection of people to be appropriate. Confucius said, 'At fifteen, I set my heart on learning.' This Association will soon be in its mid-teens, so in the development of self-government, we should be like Confucius setting his heart on learning, and strive to practice it even more. Although people have different talents, and there are differences between those who are aware early and those who are aware later, when they succeed, they are the same. If one person can do it a hundred times, and ten people can do it a thousand times, then even if one is afraid, one will surely become clear, and even if one is weak, one will surely become strong. This is in line with Sun Yat-sen's instruction to 'catch up head-on' and achieve the goal of equal treatment. Each representative of this Association bears the heavy responsibility entrusted by the taxpayers, and the earnest expectations of the government and society, and should unite and strive to live up to the world. The major work of this Association in the past year, and the efforts of the previous representatives to the Municipal Council, have been recorded in pamphlets and need not be repeated. However, among the resolutions of the first meeting of the previous representative assembly, some have already been implemented, and some have not been seen to move. For example, the music team is still not cancelled, and we really do not know why the opinions of the taxpayers are so discriminated against, which is truly bewildering. As for the education problem, it is one of the focuses of the exchange of notes on March 26th of the Republic of China year 17. Although it is progressing gradually, it is still far from the goal. Regarding the education of our Chinese people, it has been decided to simultaneously increase and subsidize it. However, although the subsidies have increased slightly year by year, the eight-year plan to increase schools has been neglected and has become an invisible situation of stagnation. It must be known that education is an important task of modern political systems, and especially the responsibility of autonomous organs. The Municipal Council has established itself in the position of a 'quasi-autonomous organ,' and must not favor one over the other. If one looks at the education budget, the comparison of school-age children, the level of teachers' salaries, and the cost per student, one can know that the statement of 'favoring one over the other' is not unfounded. According to the eight-year plan, from the Republic of China years 20 to 27, a total of 17 complete primary schools should be established, and a total of six complete middle schools should be established. The number of students entering primary school should be about 10,000, accounting for about 7% of school-age children. Under the current situation, it can barely be considered comforting. Unexpectedly, the Bureau re-examined this minimum eight-year plan, claiming financial difficulties and suspending it for one year. This Association lamented this greatly at the previous general assembly. However, considering that the local economy in recent years has indeed been inferior to before, and construction has been frequent, allowing it a little rest may also be permitted by the times. We deeply hope that after the one-year period, it will proceed according to the original plan. However, the Board of Directors did not adopt the Education Committee's proposal to add two primary schools and one girls' high school, and the education budget for this year did not include the funds for increasing schools. Then, the minimum plan has become empty talk on paper, and we really do not know what the intention is. If it is said that there is no funding, then the music team has been authorized by this Association to dissolve, but it has refused to implement it, and this year's budget still lists 244,000 yuan. It is so stingy for undertakings that seek the welfare of the majority, and so generous for settings that cater to the enjoyment of a very small number. Should the policy of a public organ be like this? As for the textbooks for middle schools, there is no need to use English entirely. For example, for mathematics, if English is used, there is no need to have it taught by English speakers, so the cost can be saved and hiring will be more convenient. This is in fundamental conflict with the content of the exchange of notes, and it is also contrary to the principles of education. This Association should take this opportunity to solemnly declare and warn the authorities in charge of the actual autonomous organs that 'the eight-year plan is the minimum education policy for our local landowners. Unless it is carried out quickly and thoroughly, there is absolutely no way to dispel the difficulties in the understanding of taxpayers, and the selection of educators should also take into account the suitability of language, habits, customs, and people.' This is a touchstone for whether the municipal authorities will cooperate sincerely from today onwards. The Special Zone Court was difficult to establish based on the agreement, but its position is completely independent. If there is any behavior that is 'inconsistent with the law,' there are legal procedures for correction, and it is a serious stain on the dignity of the court to openly attack and despise it in public places or public publications, which is a serious stain on those who pride themselves on the rule of law. As far as this Association knows, 'the Special Zone Court considers the police officers of the Municipal Council to be civil servants,' but the Municipal Council's annual report for the Republic of China year 23, on page 20, under the Special Zone Court section, states that 'the court authorities refused to recognize the police officers of the Municipal Council as civil servants,' which is inconsistent with the facts. The taxpayers must correct this erroneous understanding in the publications of impartial organs, in order to rectify public perception and avoid social misunderstandings. We hope that the Municipal Council's rulers will be extra vigilant in the future, strictly abide by the spirit of decisiveness, and maintain the dignity of the court. For the service of the previous representatives to the Municipal Council, we would like to express our deep gratitude on behalf of the taxpayers, and hope for your guidance.

Report of Directors and Committee Members The report of the directors and committee members of the Municipal Council of the Public Concession for the Republic of China year 23 stated: "We were mistakenly appointed by the previous representative assembly as directors of the Board of Directors and members of various committees of the Municipal Council for the Republic of China year 23. A year has passed, and our term is coming to an end. Today, we are pleased to attend the first meeting of the representative assembly for the Republic of China year 24. We would like to report on the matters related to our Chinese citizens that we have participated in and carried out during our term of office. (1) Distribution of duties in the Administrative Committee. The number of members of the Municipal Council's Administrative Committee this year is no different from the previous year. It is in the administrative system of the Bureau, connecting the top and bottom, and holding the key. It has been described in detail in the previous report, so there is no need to repeat it. Westerners, seeing the indifference of taxpayers towards participating in electoral politics, believe that in order to encourage the political enthusiasm of voters, it is essential to give them opportunities to participate in politics, so that everyone sees the goodness and evils of local administration as their own business, and then they will have a sense of shared weal and woe. Under the current administrative system of the concession, expanding the organization of the Administrative Committee and recruiting well-known people from all walks of life to participate in deliberations is the beginning of opening up the municipal administration. According to past practice, the most important task when new directors gather in a special meeting is to decide the number of seats and the candidates for each committee. In addition to the directors themselves allocating work and distributing the committee members elected by this Association, there have also been cases of inviting outside people to participate in the organization, but the number is not large. This is because there are concerns that the committee will become too large and its operation will not be flexible, so there are slight restrictions. Currently, there are about 30 Chinese committee members hired by the Bureau. The Chinese School Subsidy Committee is purely organized by Chinese people, and the Chinese committee members are the chairmen of the Water Price Review Committee. After the addition of Chinese committee members to the Land Committee, it has been two years now. As the municipal administration becomes more developed, the power of Chinese people to participate in politics will naturally gradually expand. Looking at the past from the present, its gradual progress can be reviewed. The Chinese candidates for the main committees are listed below: Finance Committee: 7 seats, 2 Chinese seats, held by Xu Xinliu and Wang Yansong; Police Committee: 8 seats, 3 Chinese seats, held by Yu Qiaqing, Jiang Yiping, and Xi Yushu; Works Committee: 7 seats, 3 Chinese seats, held by Yuan Ludeng, Guo Shun, and Wang Yansong; Staff Committee: 6 seats, 2 Chinese seats, held by Bei Songsun and Guo Shun; Public Utilities Committee: 7 seats, 3 Chinese seats, held by Feng Bingnan, Jiang Yiping, and Yu Hualong; Health Committee: 9 seats, 3 Chinese seats, held by Jiang Yiping, Chen Jicheng, and Yu Hualong; Transportation Committee: 9 seats, 2 Chinese seats, held by Xu Xinliu and Xi Yushu; Education Committee: 9 seats, 4 Chinese seats, held by Yuan Ludeng, Lin Kanghou, Liu Zhanen, and Ou Yuanhuai; Library Committee: 5 seats, 2 Chinese seats, held by Bei Songsun and Chen Jicheng. (2) Promotion of Chinese education. The Municipal Council's education policy, after being re-established by the Education Committee in the Republic of China year 20, is divided into two major outlines: 1. To promote Bureau-established schools; 2. To subsidize private schools. In recent years, education administration has been carried out in accordance with this. As for Westerners, let's put it aside for the time being. In terms of Chinese education, the eight-year construction plan and the designated private school subsidies are all based on this outline. The eight-year plan started to be implemented in the 20th year, and it was decided to add two primary schools every year. By the end of the 23rd year, two girls' middle schools were to be established. There are now five primary schools. Except for one on Huade Road, all have self-owned school buildings, and the scale is roughly complete. However, because the Bureau's finances have not been prosperous in recent years, it is still Zhu Keshi's plan to proceed, which is frustrating. Moreover, the original proposal was to review the entire plan by the Republic of China year 23. As a result of the review, construction was suspended for one year, which is even more regrettable. Now that the suspension period has expired, the two primary schools and one girls' middle school that should have been added this year have not been included in the budget due to the Bureau's financial difficulties, which is inevitably disappointing. Since the eight-year plan was solemnly announced by the Bureau in the past, and the plan is actually a minimum facility, we still hope that the Bureau can find other ways to promote its realization this year. In addition, the new school building of the existing girls' middle school was completed at the beginning of the year and has been moved into. The Jingzhou Road Primary School was also used to open a night school in the autumn of last year, which specializes in receiving unemployed workers and teaching them simple courses. Many people came enthusiastically. The subsidy system has been expanded year by year since its implementation. In the Republic of China year 21, the amount was only 110,000 taels of silver, and 57 schools were subsidized. The following year, the amount increased to 140,000 taels, and the number of schools also increased to 87. Last year, at the suggestion of our colleagues, it increased by 50,000 taels, totaling 190,000 taels, and the number of schools also increased to 150. This year, the number of schools has increased by another 45, and the amount has increased to 210,000 taels. As in the past, the Bureau will set up a subsidy committee to be responsible for the distribution. The Health Department will also send people to inspect, and those whose health facilities do not meet the regulations will be suspended. Last autumn, the Japanese Residents Association suggested stopping the establishment of new schools and transferring all the construction fees to subsidies. The Education Committee believed that this move was contrary to the current education policy, because the current policy stipulates that the construction of new schools and the subsidy of private schools should be carried out in two separate ways, so as not to be unbalanced. If the education construction funds are concentrated on the subsidy route, not only will there be practical disadvantages of being uneven, but the years of planning that have been effective will be abandoned in one fell swoop, which is not advisable. The Board of Directors approved its proposal, and the Japanese proposal was therefore denied. (3) Establishment of the Rickshaw Management Office. Since the establishment of the Management Office in May of last year to improve the rickshaw system, three Chinese and foreign paid committee members have been dedicated to this task. Their task is to promote 13 of the 16 items recommended by the Rickshaw Committee. The remaining three items, which relate to the recovery of car licenses and the organization of new companies, will be handled later. In the past year, achievements have been made, such as registering real car owners, organizing rickshaw pullers' mutual aid associations, and reducing car rentals, which have been quite laborious. (4) Improvement of the Public Library. The Municipal Council used to have a public library attached to the Municipal Building on Nanjing Road, commonly known as the Foreign Language College. After the sale of the Municipal Building, the books were moved to No. 22 Nanjing Road and opened as usual. The library has books and newspapers for people to browse, but they are mostly in Western languages, which is inconvenient for Chinese people. Therefore, there have been repeated proposals to add Chinese classics. According to the library's funding, except for a small portion borne by regular users, the rest is allocated from donations and taxes, and the income from donations and taxes is mainly from our Chinese people. Our Chinese citizens account for the vast majority of the population in the concession, so it is reasonable and necessary to collect and include Chinese classics. Currently, the library has 3,800 volumes of Chinese books, which were donated by Mr. Yan E-sheng, the secretary of this Association. The volumes are quite numerous and carefully selected. The person in charge has compiled a catalog for easy reference. Our citizens can go to read them at any time after work. In this year's budget, a part has been allocated for the purchase of new books and newspapers for the purpose of increasing Chinese books and newspapers. The catalog of new books is published in the Chinese Public Gazette on a regular basis, so you can pay attention to reading it. In order to encourage Chinese people's interest in the library, the Bureau has ordered the Information Department to widely disseminate the news of adding Chinese books, and painted large Chinese characters in front of the library as a guide. The library has a suggestion book on a regular basis, so readers can sign their opinions on the books to be purchased and other matters to be reformed at any time for adoption. If the number of Chinese readers gradually increases in the future, and the use of Chinese books becomes more and more widespread, the funds for adding Chinese books and newspapers will naturally increase year by year, without saying a word. The library's opening hours are set from 8:30 am to 8:00 pm every day. On Sundays, it will be changed to start at 10:00 am and still at the afternoon. (5) Key policies of public health. There are three things to pay attention to in the concession's health administration: (1) Donating funds for the construction of the Beiqiao Town Mental Hospital. In July of last year, Mr. Lu Bohong represented the hospital and asked the Municipal Council to donate construction funds. The Bureau decided to donate 100,000 yuan to designate several beds specifically for accommodating patients in the concession, on the condition that the Municipal Government and the French Concession authorities would donate together. Now the Municipal Government has donated 100,000 yuan, and the French Concession's Public Board of Directors has also donated 50,000 yuan. The Bureau's 100,000 yuan has also been issued. Patients can be accommodated in May. The establishment of the mental hospital is in line with the needs of the times and is of great benefit to public health. It is gratifying that the Bureau and the Municipal Government have worked together to achieve this. (2) Adopting the recommendations of the Milk Committee. The Milk Committee was organized and established a year ago. Last year, it drafted a report, which was revised by the Health Committee and approved by the Board of Directors for adoption. The main motion was the issue of milk and cream disinfection. All proposals to organize a municipal disinfection plant were rejected by the committee. (3) Conducting school health inspections. School health inspections are an essential policy to protect the health of the nation. The Municipal Government has been implementing it for a long time. The Municipal Council's schools also started to implement it last year. It is organized by the Health Department and started with Chinese children's primary schools. The Huaide Road, Jingzhou Road, North District, and East District primary schools have been inspected, with a total of more than 2,600 students. Special attention is paid to trachoma and free treatment is provided. Other diseases are either diagnosed by private doctors or temporarily suspended from school to go home for recuperation. The scale of the inspection office has been slightly expanded this year. Although the scope is small, it is not without results. (6) Consideration of telephone price increases. The telephone business in the concession was previously handled by the China-Foreign German Telephone Company, but the results were unsatisfactory. Since the Shanghai Telephone Company took over in the Republic of China year 19, it applied to the Municipal Council the year before last for permission to increase prices, but the Bureau rejected it. This year, it re-applied for the previous request. The reason it gave was that according to the provisions of the patent contract, the company should get a net profit of 10% annual interest. Taking last year as an example, after deducting income and expenditure, the net profit was only slightly more than 6% of the investment amount, which was far from the amount of guaranteed interest. It should be allowed to increase prices by about 23% from April of this year and implement new charging rules. All commercial telephones will be charged according to the number of calls, and other types will be increased or decreased according to the current price. As soon as the news of the price increase was heard, Chinese and foreign groups raised objections. According to the company's calculation of various items of profit and loss, such as the payment of US government income tax and the management fee of the International Telegraph and Telephone Company, were listed under the expenditure items, which resulted in a sudden increase in expenditure, and the operating income was not enough to pay the guaranteed interest. There is room for discussion on all of these. The income tax item was not within the scope of the contract, so it should not be rejected by the users. That is, the management fee paid to the International Company (calculated at 4.5% of the total income per year, which requires about 300,000 yuan) should not be burdened by Shanghai for a long time. As for the depreciation item, the Bureau had previously lent to help the company at the end of the year before last to change the debt from gold to silver. Therefore, the number of investment aspects should be reduced by 3 million yuan, and the amount of annual depreciation can also be greatly reduced. The cash case is still under careful consideration. During this period of economic decline, everything that can avoid increasing the burden on citizens should be fully committed to. (7) Negotiations on the return of roads built beyond the boundary. The negotiations on the return of roads built beyond the boundary have been intermittent and have not been resolved. Although the draft agreement has been drafted, the opinions of the two sides are difficult to agree on suddenly. There are about two things: (1) The four boundaries of the area where the agreement is implemented; (2) The organization of the special police station and the number of police officers. There are many practical difficulties in determining the four boundaries, which need to be resolved urgently. Although the number of police officers and the nationality of police officers seem to be easier, they still cost a lot of effort. Last October, the two sides resumed negotiations. After several consultations, significant progress has been made in all the points listed in the agreement. What is particularly gratifying is that the public utility companies in the concession have completed negotiations with the Municipal Government on the issuance of patent contracts for the area where roads are built beyond the boundary. However, business development still depends on the resolution of the entire issue of roads built beyond the boundary. (8) The financial situation of the concession. The main sources of income for the Municipal Council's finances are the general municipal tax, the land tax, the wharf tax, and the license tax. In the past, the local economy was prosperous and the tax sources were excellent, so all municipal development plans could be carried out step by step. In addition to balancing revenue and expenditure in the annual budget, there was often a surplus. The general municipal tax is now 14% of the rent value. Several years ago, it was increased by 2%. Later, the electricity department was sold, and 8.1 million taels of silver were obtained. The city treasury suddenly became wealthy, and the additional 2% tax was abolished. This was the matter of the Republic of China year 19. In recent years, the municipal administration has developed day by day, and the balance of revenue and expenditure is often lost. Although there have been proposals to increase taxes from time to time, the local business situation is declining compared to the past, and the rise and fall of the economy are really important. We cannot burden the people's livelihood, so this proposal has been made and withdrawn several times. We still focus on reducing expenditure to cultivate tax sources and temporarily alleviate the people's difficulties. Last year, because various administrative offices made a lot of efforts to tighten their belts, and as a result of the silver being expensive and the gold being cheap, the budget expenditure could be reduced. Therefore, the total revenue and expenditure of the annual final account were balanced, and there was a surplus of 1.1 million taels of silver. However, the tax revenue was also 430,000 taels short, and the 45,000 yuan of the Rickshaw Management Office was not originally in the budget. Therefore, the net surplus was about 700,000 yuan. We had previously predicted that only 40,000 yuan could be left over. Now we have obtained this number, which is very gratifying. As for this year's (i.e., the Republic of China year 24) budget, the regular expenditure is about 27 million yuan, and the tax revenue is about 25.9 million yuan. The shortfall is about 1.2 million yuan. As in the past, it will be allocated from the public accumulation fund to maintain its balance. The increase in taxes can be postponed again. The abundance of public tax revenue is closely related to the prosperity of the local economy. In recent years, the business situation has been depressed and the people's livelihood has been difficult. The municipal administration should also focus on saving money. Last year's surplus exceeded expectations, and this year's revenue and expenditure can be balanced again. It is comforting to be able to report this during this period of economic decline. (9) Improvement of the transportation system. Shanghai is an important hub for sea and land transportation. It is located in an important place with a dense population and heavy traffic. The traffic in the city is very congested, and the development of the area is increasing. Therefore, how to circulate traffic, facilitate pedestrians, and has become an important policy today. The Bureau has made every effort to carry out the work. Within the possible financial resources, it has given priority to acquiring private land and expanding the road surface. This year alone, the purchase of land at the corner of Henan Road and Nanjing Road cost 300,000 yuan, which can be seen in general. There are many other roads that need to be widened. It is not only not allowed by the city treasury to do it all at once, but also because the owners do not have any renovation plans, they cannot be forced to move and buy at a price. Therefore, they can only proceed step by step and determine the priority according to the urgency of the needs. Other improvement measures, such as adding traffic lights, revising parking regulations, and designating one-way traffic routes, are all being carried out step by step. The one-way traffic that is inconvenient for merchants, such as the area around Hankou Road, has been changed. In addition, attention has been paid to the cooperation between public buses and trams at various stations to facilitate passengers, and double-decker public buses have been added to avoid congestion, all of which have been somewhat effective. The Chief of the Police Department is currently on leave, and the Bureau is providing him with convenience to investigate the latest transportation methods in Europe and the United States for adoption. As for transportation issues that have a consistent nature throughout the city, the three-sector authorities will hold joint meetings to seek cooperation and jointly solve them. Shanghai's administration is divided into three districts, so each key policy has its own system. Transportation is one example. If the three parties can cooperate and plan a unified transportation network, then it will be a great benefit to our citizens. The above are the recordable events in the concession's administration in the past year, and they are particularly closely related to Chinese people. I have described the beginning and the end to inform you. The Municipal Council's annual report and gazette have been published in Chinese for many years. The key policies in the boundary are disclosed from time to time. The Chinese annual report was only one-third of the English version when it was first published. This year's translation is more detailed and has many volumes. This Association will send them to taxpayers for reading. Everything that is omitted in this report is detailed in the report. Since we have taken office, we have been afraid of failure. Fortunately, we have been encouraged by you from time to time, so that we can work hard to go. We are still ashamed that we cannot live up to the expectations of the citizens. Please forgive us. Reported by Directors Yu Qiaqing, Yuan Ludeng, Bei Zuyi, Xu Xinliu, Jiang Yiping, Committee Members Lin Kanghou, Guo Shun, Wang Yansong, Xi Yushu, Chen Jicheng, and Yu Hualong, April 16, Republic of China year 24.

Guangdong Province: Northeastern Guangdong Suffers Severe Flooding; The Southern Section of the Yuehan Railway Is Submerged; Huizhou Is Greatly Inundated, and Boluo County Experiences Levee Failure 98

Guangzhou dispatch: Various areas of Guangdong Province have experienced continuous heavy rains for over a month, leading to a sudden surge in river levels across the northeast, west, and other regions. The situation is particularly severe in the northeast, resulting in widespread flooding. Residents in the affected areas are actively evacuating, facing considerable hardship, and causing food prices to rise dramatically, creating a genuine disaster. Upon investigation, the Beijiang River channel is naturally shallow and narrow, causing the river to overflow regularly during the two rainy seasons. This time, heavy rains in Hunan Province flowed towards Guangdong, and the waters of the Xiaobeijiang River also drained into the Beijiang. With the combined rainwater, the Beijiang River has swelled even further, with Shaozhou, Yingde, Qingyuan, and other counties bearing the initial impact. Starting from the 7th of this month, the areas along the southern section of the Yuehan Railway, including Shaoguan, Maba, Yingde, and Xiangjiangkou, have been transformed into a vast swamp. The water level is approximately nine feet higher than normal. The Junqiao bridge outside the south gate of Shaozhou and a wooden bridge near Yingde have been destroyed by the flood, disrupting transportation. The water depth in Shaocheng is several feet, requiring pedestrians to use boats for movement. Yingde's terrain is lower than Shaozhou, so the floodwaters in Yingde City are about seven or eight feet high, having already reached the upper floors of residences. Most residents have temporarily moved to higher ground for safety, resulting in significant losses of furniture and goods. The water flow at Xiangjiangkou is becoming increasingly rapid. From Shaozhou to Xiangjiangkou, passing through the various stations in Yingde, the view is an endless expanse of water. The Yuehan Railway's roadbed is only nine feet above the water surface, and if the floodwaters rise another foot, trains will be unable to operate. Therefore, the Yuehan Railway Bureau has been exceptionally busy with flood prevention work in recent days. On the 10th, a mountain flood occurred near Yingde Station, causing earth to collapse and block the railway tracks, leading to train stoppages. Fortunately, engineering personnel were dispatched immediately to clear the mud, and train service was restored in the afternoon. According to reports from the Railway Bureau's special envoy, this flood on the Beijiang River exceeds the flood of 1919 by twenty-eight feet, breaking all previous records. The government, upon receiving the report, has instructed the Qujiang, Yingde, Qingyuan, and other county governments to implement flood prevention measures and provide relief to the refugees. Various charitable organizations in Guangzhou have also dispatched personnel carrying relief supplies to provide assistance in the disaster areas. On the eastern front, torrential rains also began on the 7th of this month, lasting for three consecutive days and nights, causing the water level to rise sharply. On the 8th, the water level was over nine feet, and by the 9th, it had exceeded ten feet. The lower reaches of Boluo and Huizhou have become greatly inundated, and the water flow is ceaseless. The Shuitangwei area in Boluo County breached on the same day, with a gap of several feet, resulting in the inundation of all villages within the area. All villagers from three townships and one administrative unit fled to the hills for safety, with dozens of houses collapsing due to the flood. On the 10th, the water level rose another four feet. The Shuimen Village, Shaxia Township, and Xiapu Township along the Dongjiang River in Huizhou have been transformed into a vast swamp, with fields and farmland completely submerged. In Huiyang County, the areas of Shaibuchang, Xiami Street, and Mupaixia in the county seat have water depths that reach the shin, and residents are actively moving furniture to the upper floors to prevent losses. Outside Boluo County, the water level in Mupaixia and Hongsheng Temple has reached the knee, requiring residents to travel by boat. The construction of the Tonghu dike has been halted recently, and the surrounding fields and crops along the river have been submerged by the flood, making a poor early harvest predictable. The water level of the Xijiang River showed little change before the 9th. However, after the 10th, as the floodwaters of the Beijiang River flowed in, the waters of the Xijiang River could not flow freely, causing the water level in Sihui, Zhaoqing, and other counties to rise by two to three feet. The water level at the Hekou section in Sanshui County is level with the embankment, and the rapid current makes navigation dangerous. Fortunately, the floodwaters from Guizhou Province have not yet arrived, so the water level has not increased drastically. If the waters of the Beijiang River can be discharged within a few days, the Xijiang River may avoid becoming a major disaster like the northeastern rivers. (April 12th)

Baoshan: Luodian Holds a God-Worshipping Festival 99

The twenty-odd temples in Luodian Town, in response to the severe drought last year that led to rural bankruptcy, have jointly initiated a god-worshipping festival (commonly known as "jiehuangqian") to pray for abundant harvests and the well-being of the people. Preparations have been underway for over a month. Hundreds of so-called large and small gold and silver ingots have been made, with the largest being over ten feet tall and several feet wide. Various flags, umbrellas, and ceremonial paraphernalia have been collected exhaustively. Rare and ancient treasures are also on display in the various temples. In recent days, crowds have been flocking to the town from distant places to offer incense. The festival is scheduled to begin at 1:00 PM on the 18th of this month (Thursday). This type of festival was held once twenty years ago, and the grand occasion caused a stir at that time.

Songjiang: The Red Cross Society Sends Zhejiang Refugees Back to Their Hometowns 100

Since last winter, the Songjiang Red Cross Society established a reception center for drought refugees from Zhejiang Province. From March 25th to April 3rd of this year, the refugees who were kept and cared for were sent back to their hometowns in batches with cars allocated by the Railway Bureau after commercial negotiation. There were more than 10,400 people in total. In recent days, more than 1,200 Zhejiang drought victims scattered in the four rural areas have come to Songjiang one after another, asking to be sent back. The Society again negotiated with the Railway Bureau for vehicles and on the night train on the 15th of this month, Zhou Xuewen, the director of the Society, escorted them back to their hometowns by car. At the same time, 100 stones of relief rice were raised from the Jiaxu All-Zhejiang Early Disaster Relief Association and other organizations, and relief tickets were issued so that the refugees would be issued one stone of relief rice each by name after they were sent to the stone, half for children, to avoid starvation.

The Central Inspection Group Visits Songjiang 101

The Central Party Department inspection group arrived in Songjiang from Shanghai on the morning of the 16th. The members were Zhang Beihai, Zheng Bohao, He Qisang, and Hong Shucai, four people from the Investigation Section of the Organization Committee. After arriving at the County Party Department, they immediately summoned the executive and supervisory committee members to listen to the work report. Then, they summoned all the staff to talk separately and inspect the interior. Then, accompanied by Party Committee members Wang Zhewu, Sun Shiheng, and Lu Shulian, they went to the library, the public education hall, the first district Party Department, the first district office, the County Chamber of Commerce and other places to inspect, and went to the Xin Songjiang Society Restaurant for dinner, and then took the 6 o'clock express train to Shanghai.

Taicang: Robbery in Weaving Shoe Village 102

The home of Wang Shunqing, a resident of Zhilü Township in the sixth district of the county, was suddenly visited by more than a dozen bandits on the night before yesterday. Speaking in a Hakka accent, they carried guns and other weapons, broke down the door and entered, overturning boxes and cabinets, searching arbitrarily. After about an hour, they swaggered away. After checking, it was found that jewelry such as beaded flowers, gold bracelets, and gold rings, worth about 500 yuan, had been robbed. The matter has been reported by the victim to the fifth police station of the public security, which has been reported to the County Bureau, requesting that personnel be sent to investigate and arrest the perpetrators.

Wuxi: Yang Qinghe Silver Shop Robbed and Injured 103

Datieqiao Street in the north gate of the city is a prosperous area in the northern commercial district. At the southern end of the bridge, there is a Yang Qinghe Silver Shop, managed by Zhang Shanqing from Jian County. The business is good. It was robbed once seven or eight years ago, but the case has not been solved. The shop staff and shareholders are all from the Ningbo gang. The night before last (the 15th) at 8:15 PM, just as the market was closing, three robbers suddenly came, speaking in a Zhejiang-Wuxi accent. Two robbers entered the shop, claiming they wanted to buy a gold bracelet, and one robber was on the lookout outside. Shop assistant Ji Zunhua came out to negotiate and invited one robber to the reception room to talk, and ordered apprentice Shen Zhichun to take out a pair of twisted silk and flat bracelets from the back warehouse, weighing three and a half taels. Unexpectedly, the robber pulled out a pistol from his sleeve and fired a shot at Ji Zunhua, causing Ji's left arm to be shot. Bleeding profusely, he hid in pain. The shop staff were all frightened and stood like wooden chickens. The robber then snatched the gold bracelet into his pocket, rushed out the door, and fled towards the Yingxiangqiao Daochang Alley. Afterwards, Hong Houchang, the director of the first public security bureau in charge, Zhong Jizuo, the captain of the public security bureau's investigation team, Wu Zhengrong, the chief of political police of the county government, and Xu Yi, the attached officer of the sixth security brigade, all received the news one after another and personally led armed police teams to investigate. An empty shell of a pistol bullet was found. The situation was tense at the time, and a temporary curfew was announced, as if facing a great enemy. Half of the five city gates were closed, and pedestrians entering and leaving were searched. Police were sent to check in the thatched sheds, but it was all in vain and nothing was found. The wounded man was sent to the Tongren Hospital by the shop manager for treatment. The injury was slight and there was no danger to his life. Also, Zhou Wu, a woman from Sheng Alley under Xiaoyanjiapeng in the fourth district, was also robbed of a gold ring by bandits with guns near Longshanshao. However, the bandit Sun Aying was arrested on the spot. In the case of Wang Shiyi, a resident of the town, who encountered bandits at Jiuliji, the director of the third bureau, Dang Zhongyue, arrested the bandits Zhu Xiaofengzi and Wang Xiaosi yesterday and sent them to the bureau for interrogation.

Adultery Leads to Murder 104

Chen Daguan's eldest son, Agou, in Shenwan, Huazhuang Township, District 264, is 21 years old and works as a waterman. He is honest and straightforward and has not yet married. However, he has already engaged a Miss Shen from Shenxi Alley as his wife and plans to marry next year. Shen Meisheng, a neighbor on the left, is a businessman in Shanghai. His wife, Ms. Mou, is very romantic and unwilling to sleep alone. She is familiar with Afu, the son of Chen Renquan nearby. On the 4th of this month, Afu planned to go to Shen's house to continue the fun, but Agou found out and followed him, calling out to catch the adulterer and deliberately making fun of him, which angered Afu. So he ran out and grabbed Agou, beating him severely, causing serious injuries. After Agou returned home, he was bedridden and his injuries worsened day by day. He vomited blood and died in the middle of the night on the 12th of this month. Zou Shiling, the head of the district, reported the matter to the local branch court. Yesterday (the 16th) morning, Prosecutor Shen led officials to the countryside to inspect the body and determined that he had died of injuries sustained before his death. After the examination, because the murderer was on the run, he ordered the family of the deceased to collect the body and wait for the arrest of the murderer for investigation.

Haimen: Qidong Yongchang Town Cracks Down on Bandit Den 106

Gu Tinghua's son Guoxian, a villager in Qidong Guangyi Village, was kidnapped by bandits on the night of the 31st of last month. Judgment in Embezzlement and Murder Case 107

Sun Yuanfu, a resident of Changchun Town, District 3, was arrested and shot by Ni Yueqiu, the former head of the fifth district, in the spring of 1919 on suspicion of being a bandit. Now, Sun's wife, Shen, sued Ni in the Shanghai District Court for the crime of embezzlement and murder. The court arrested and detained Ni, and Prosecutor Ouyang Shu investigated and found the facts to be true and filed a public prosecution. On the 6th of this month, Criminal Court President Sun Enrong opened the court to interrogate him once. On the morning of the day before yesterday (12th), Ni Yueqiu was sentenced to sixteen years in prison. It is said that Ni did not accept the judgment and appealed to the High Court yesterday (14th).

Qingjiang: Notorious Bandit Zhang Zhigao Executed by Firing Squad 108

The notorious bandit Zhang Zhigao has been causing trouble in the counties of Huai, Lian, Ye, Shu, Fu, Ning, and Yancheng for many years. He has repeatedly resisted the garrison troops, relying on his gang to resist arrest, and has never been captured. The people of each county have long regarded him as a tiger. In recent years, he has looted Yilin in Funing and Guzhai in Lianshui, devastating the area and causing thousands or tens of thousands of dollars in damage to the people. It is even more difficult to count the number of lives lost. He was arrested in Shanghai by the Jiangsu Provincial Security Command and escorted to Pu on the evening of the 13th and temporarily detained in the Seventh District Security Command. This (14th) morning, Chief of Staff Li Fuzhen extracted the bandit, verified his identity, and tied him to the Nancheng School Ground for execution by firing squad.

Nantong: Coastal Yellow Croaker Fishing Flourishes 109

The coast of Jiangbei is now in the peak season for yellow croaker fishing. In Lvsi, Juegang, and Jiaogang, the number of fishing boats going to sea has exceeded one thousand. In previous years, sea bandits caused disturbances, and fishermen were extorted more than 300,000 yuan in so-called flag fees during the fishing season. This year, special strong men were drawn from the fishermen for self-defense.

Jiaxing: Fourth Branch Director Suspended 111

Xu Hongxiang, the director of the fourth public security branch in Jiaxing, has been in office for many years. Recently, Xu's residence was burglarized, and Xu suspected Zhang Yiqin, a worker at the Xinning Temple, and used torture to force a confession. Zhang then sued the local branch court for assault and filed a complaint with the Provincial Department to investigate. The assault case has been concluded and the verdict will be announced soon. A few days ago, Guo Jianshi and other townspeople listed ten items and filed a complaint with the authorities. After Cheng Taichang, an inspector sent by the county, went to verify each item, Xu was suspended on the 15th and He Zhanfeng was appointed to take over immediately, and the transfer was limited to immediate.

Statistics of Opium Smokers in the County 112

Jiaxing is located at the intersection of Jiangsu and Zhejiang and the main road between Shanghai and Hangzhou. Smuggling and private transport of opium are easy to mix in. Although the authorities have strictly investigated and banned it, it is difficult to eliminate it completely. Now, Wu Wangji, the special commissioner for smoking ban, believes that the number of opium smokers in Jiaxing County accounts for about 15 per thousand of the total population, and the money spent on drugs every year is more than 500,000 yuan, which is quite alarming. He has listed it and reported it to the province and ordered the county to strictly investigate and ban it to eliminate the opium poison.

Exchanging and Distributing Native Seeds for Breeding 113

Jiaxing silkworm farming has entered the stage of urging greening. Each guidance station has scheduled to distribute seedlings on the 20th, but the disaster victims in the fifth district have stopped breeding due to lack of funds to purchase seeds. Now, in order to provide relief to the disaster victims, the county government has specially distributed more than 10,000 local seeds that have been exchanged back to the disaster victims in the district for breeding, so as to revitalize silkworm farming.

Vendetta Occurs in Rural Areas of the Sixth District 114

Ding Sishi, a farmer from Zhangshi Village, Shiwang Township, Sixth District of Jiaxing, was working in the field at 3:00 PM on the 15th when he suddenly heard a gunshot, so he paid attention to watch. He only saw a boat coming from the east in the river port in the south. A person on the boat was holding a quick gun and shooting at the shore. A child in the boat shouted "Daddy" frantically. After a while, the boat left. Ding then went to check and saw an unknown man, about 50 years old, wearing a blue cloth short jacket and blue cotton pants, with a bullet wound in his abdomen. Ding Sishi reported the incident to the local police station, and patrol chief Chen Ruizhang went to inspect the scene. The corpse was entrusted to the village chief Zhu Shunguan for proper care and reported to Zheng Hui, the director of the Sixth Branch Bureau, who then reported to the court for an examination. According to general speculation, the shooting was a vendetta.

The night sailing ship from Shaoxing Hao to Kaixixing was intercepted by a robber ship at night on the 14th near Nanjianqing. Nine robbers jumped out, ordered the ship to stop, and searched all 21 male and female passengers with knives and clubs. Clothing and silver were lost, worth approximately 200 silver dollars.
