Annual Meeting of Foreign Taxpayers to Be Held at Grand Cathay Theatre 116

The annual meeting of foreign taxpayers, originally scheduled to be held at the Carlton Theatre by the Public Works Department, has now been decided to be held at the Grand Cathay Theatre due to the smaller size of the Carlton Theatre. The meeting will be held today (April 17) starting at 5:00 PM.

T.V. Soong Expresses Optimism About the Financial Future; Chinese and Foreign Banks Are Willing to Cooperate with Us; The Government Guarantees There Will Be No Inflation 117

National News Agency Shanghai, April 16: T.V. Soong, Chairman of the Board of Directors of the Bank of China, in view of some inaccuracies in the draft of his speech issued by a news agency today, has specially submitted his official speech draft to the National News Agency for publication as follows. Mr. Soong first stated that my country is indeed encountering great difficulties, but we must remain calm, because the world is in an economic recession. Shanghai has suffered the most, but my country is based on agriculture, and the adverse effects on farmers are still manageable. Shanghai's prosperity must ultimately rely on the mainland. The situation in the mainland is greatly improving, and Shanghai will definitely benefit from it, which is really gratifying. Mr. Soong continued that he had informally exchanged views with some Chinese and foreign bankers, and the results were very moving, because they were all able to cooperate to deal with this common problem, regardless of Chinese or foreign. This is also gratifying. In addition, the Minister of Finance adheres to his sound financial and sound fiscal policies, which is very important. At this point, Mr. Soong reaffirmed that he had obtained a government guarantee that there would be no inflation. Looking at the above factors, we are very optimistic about the future. As for the US continuing to raise the price of silver from 64 cents to 71 cents, Mr. Soong said that this will of course increase my country's difficulties, but the method of strictly prohibiting the private smuggling of raw silver exports is now quite effective, so there will be no panic in Shanghai. Central News Agency said that T.V. Soong, Standing Committee Member of the National Economic Council and Chairman of the Board of Directors of the Bank of China, met with reporters from various newspapers at the Bank of China at 10:00 AM yesterday and made the following remarks.

Foreign Banks Express Cooperation

According to Mr. Soong, since taking office as Chairman of the Board of Directors of the Bank of China, he has not had any exchanges with the foreign banking community, so he invited the foreign banking community to lunch on the 14th (reporter's note: Soong's residence denied this on that day). The attendees included the managers of HSBC, Citibank, Chartered, Credit Lyonnais, Mitsubishi, and Yokohama Specie Bank, as well as Messrs. Seidel and Beisson. During the meeting, informal exchanges of views were made on financial issues, and the results were quite good. Everyone present was able to focus on finance and put their own interests aside, and cooperate fully. They also expressed their willingness not to export silver automatically on the silver issue. I have conveyed the results of the exchange of views to Minister of Finance Kong.

No Large-Scale Export of Silver

Regarding the question of whether the silver export equalization tax needs to be increased, this matter is within the authority of the Ministry of Finance. I am in the position of the banking community and obey the Ministry of Finance in everything, so it is not convenient to express my opinion. However, as far as I know, there has been no large-scale export of silver recently. The government is still constantly expressing to the US government that this kind of action is really harmful to China. So far, there has been no other new action. According to reports, Belgian Prime Minister Qi Lande is preparing to launch a conference to promote the restabilization of the world's major currencies. I am not very clear about the content of this conference, but Mr. Qi Lande has taught in the United States for many years, and his thinking may be close to that of President Roosevelt.

I Hope the People of the Country Will Deal With It Calmly

I observe that there is absolutely no reason for panic in my country's financial future. If you believe in ghosts, you will see ghosts. I hope the people of the country will deal with it calmly and not disturb themselves. Regarding the relief of industrial and commercial borrowing, it has been decided to use 5 million as commercial credit loans and 15 million as industrial and commercial mortgage loans. As for how the banks will allocate them, it has not yet been determined. In the future, the Bank of China will do its best to handle it. The National Economic Council currently has no plans for the entire financial sector. I am scheduled to go to Beijing for a line within the day to discuss it.

Merger of the Three Banks Is Absolutely Impossible

A reporter from Xin Sheng News asked that some people advocated that the Central, China, and Communications Banks should be merged to concentrate their strength and establish a large bank to cope with the Chinese economic environment. Mr. Soong said that the businesses of the three banks are different. The Central Bank is the bank of banks, the Bank of China is the international exchange bank, and the Bank of Communications is the industrial bank. Their natures are completely different. For example, the Central Bank absolutely does not engage in ordinary banking business. Judging from this, how can the three banks merge? This is absolutely impossible.

Twenty Million Dollar Loan Release: Awaiting Ministry of Finance Order for Consultation on Implementation. Over 300 Million Dollars of Silver Reserves in Shanghai Stabilize the Public Mind; Foreign Banks Resolved Yesterday Not to Export Silver 118

A dispatch from Xin Xin News Agency reports that following the decision to release twenty million dollars in loans to aid industry and commerce, the market atmosphere has shown signs of activity. The Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications are awaiting instructions from the Ministry of Finance in Shanghai before jointly consulting with the Bankers' Association to discuss implementation methods. The Bankers' Association has already raised a credit loan fund of 1,885,000 dollars, which will be incorporated into the overall operation. Yesterday, the equalization tax rate remained unchanged, and exchange rates slightly lengthened. Details are as follows:

Twenty Million Dollars Subscribed by Various Banks

As a result of discussions between Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi and the financial community, it was decided to use fifteen million dollars for factory mortgage loans and five million dollars for credit guarantee loans. The source of these twenty million dollars has attracted considerable attention. A reporter from Xin Xin News Agency visited yesterday a bank executive who attended the financial meeting the day before. According to the executive, the twenty million dollar loan release will await instructions from the Ministry of Finance in Shanghai, after which the Central Bank will preside over consultations with the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and member banks of the Bankers' Association to discuss implementation methods. The source of the funds will primarily be the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications, with other banks acting as backup. Whether a banking syndicate will be formed, or whether the three banks will be responsible for handling the loans, will be decided after further consultations.

Credit Loans Incorporated into Operation

The Bankers' Association's credit loan program, organized through local associations and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, had already secured 1,885,000 dollars in pledges from member banks (5,000 dollars was added by a certain bank yesterday). Due to various reasons, the loan release had been delayed. According to news from the Bankers' Association yesterday, the government has now decided to release twenty million dollars in loans to aid industry and commerce. Fortunately, the goals are aligned, and the Bankers' Association intends to incorporate the funds it has raised into the five million dollar credit guarantee loan portion of the twenty million dollar loan, rather than organizing a separate operation, to simplify procedures.

Industry and Commerce Express Satisfaction

According to sources in industry and commerce, in order to seek relief, Shanghai's industrial and commercial sectors had requested that the financial community provide property mortgage and credit loans. The Ministry of Finance has consulted with the financial community and decided to provide twenty million dollars for factory mortgage and credit guarantee loans. Although the amount is less than originally requested, given the urgent need for relief in industry and commerce, having twenty million dollars of circulating funds will be of great benefit. It is hoped that the authorities and the financial community will implement the plan as soon as possible to rescue industry and commerce and stabilize the market.

Exchange Rates Slightly Lengthened, Equalization Tax Unchanged

The Foreign Exchange Equalization Committee met at 10:00 AM yesterday and decided to maintain the equalization tax rate at 6.75%, the same as before. The Central Bank's telegraphic transfer selling prices, announced yesterday, all showed a lengthening of exchange rates. New York: one hundred national currency units is 39.6875 US dollars, an increase of 0.3125 US dollars from the previous day's 39.375 US dollars. Paris: one hundred national currency units is 600 francs, an increase of six francs from the previous day. According to the Economic Research Office of the Central Bank, the total silver reserves of Chinese and foreign banks in Shanghai last week was 337,156 (unit: thousands of dollars, same below). Chinese banks held 286,792, while foreign banks held only 50,364, accounting for only one-sixth of the total. The total for Chinese and foreign banks the previous week was 334,696, indicating that the silver reserves of Chinese banks are steadily increasing.

Art Exhibition: Ninth Day of the Preview - Continued Arrival of Valuable Items, Explanation of Fees, and Difficulties Involved 119

Yesterday (April 16th) was the ninth day of the Shanghai preview for the International Exhibition of Chinese Art held in London. A continuous stream of Chinese and Western ladies visited the exhibition. The following is an account of the news obtained yesterday:

Group Tickets Limited to Morning Hours

In order to give preferential treatment to schools and academic and artistic groups, the exhibition has established a preferential measure, issuing half-price group tickets at one dollar per person. However, these group tickets are valid only in the morning, except on Mondays when the exhibition is open in the afternoon. They cannot be used in the afternoon and will be invalid after the expiration date. The exhibition is issuing this statement to remind those who purchase group tickets.

Attention to This Preview Exhibition

This Shanghai preview of Chinese art contains approximately one thousand ancient artifacts, all from past dynasties, mostly collected by the Ming and Qing emperors. These are items rarely seen by the public, so their value is evident. The items are displayed in chronological order, making them very easy to view. As a result, it is receiving much attention from all sides. The Tianjin Ta Kung Pao published a special edition dedicated to the art exhibition preview, and the Shen Bao Pictorial Weekly also featured photographs of the exhibition's products. Various illustrated magazines are competing to contact the exhibition and request permission to print photographs of the various ancient artifacts. Yesterday, the Central Propaganda Committee also sent representatives to contact the exhibition about photography matters. The Shanghai General Post Office has also requested the exhibition to produce and sell postcards featuring photographs of the ancient artifacts. The exhibition is currently considering the matter.

Minister Wang Visited the Exhibition Yesterday

Minister of Education Wang Shijie arrived in Shanghai on the express train from Nanjing at 11:00 PM on the 15th. He visited the exhibition yesterday morning (April 16th) and met with the exhibition's Director-General Yang Zhensheng and Executive Director Lei Zhen to discuss all matters. Wang also attended the annual meeting of the English-Speaking Union held at the Ducheng Hotel at 180 Jiangxi Road yesterday.

List of Newly Arrived Items

The Chinese catalogue of newly arrived items has been printed by the exhibition and is excerpted below: (A) Calligraphy and Painting: (1) Album of Flower Sketches by Diao Guangyin of the Five Dynasties, on plain paper; (2) Silk-Reeling Picture by Liu Songnian of the Song Dynasty, on paper. (B) Furniture: (1) Zitan Wood Throne Inlaid with Cloisonné Clouds, made of Zitan wood; (2) Zitan Wood Screen Inlaid with Cloisonné Immortal Mountain Pavilions, made of Zitan wood; (3) Mahogany Desk, originally named Liu Kuang's Table, made of mahogany. (C) Stationery: (1) Two Small Bone-Tube Writing Brushes; (2) White Jade Carved Pine Brush Holder; (3) Qianlong Style Fish-Shaped Imperial Inkstick; (4) White Jade Brush Rest with Wooden Base; (5) White Jade Eight-Trigram Ink Paste Box; (6) Three White Jade Seals with Wooden Box; (7) Song Dynasty Chengni Stone Qiongqu Inkstone with Wooden Base and Lid; (8) White Jade Five-Child Brush Rack with Carved Base; (9) White Jade Melon-Shaped Water Container with Jade Water Spoon; (10) Ming Dynasty Carved Lacquer Round Box; (11) Song Dynasty Ge Kiln Moon-White Lotus Petal Vase with Wooden Base, originally named Song Ge Kiln Awl-Handle Vase; (12) White Jade Tube Brush with Jade Brush Cap; (13) Boxwood Carved Plum Blossom Armrest. The above are all from the collection of the Palace Museum in Anhui. (D) Rare Ancient Books (Continued Delivery of Ancient Books from the Peiping Library): (1) Avatamsaka Sutra, Six Dynasties Manuscript, Translated by Buddhabhadra, Dunhuang Mogao Caves Collection, One of the Ancient Manuscript Rolls; (2) Mahaparinirvana Sutra, Six Dynasties Manuscript, Translated by Dharmakshema, Dunhuang Mogao Caves Collection, One of the Ancient Manuscript Rolls; (3) Dharani Sutra, Five Dynasties Carved Edition, This Scroll Was Unearthed from Leifeng Pagoda in Hangzhou; (4) Selections of Refined Literature, Northern Song Carved Edition, This Edition Is Definitely the Rensong Tiansheng Supervised Edition, the Earliest Extant Edition of the Book; (5) Comprehensive Mirror for Governing Aid, Compiled by Wang Qinruo et al. of the Song Dynasty, Northern Song Mid-Period Meishan Carved Edition; (6) Literary Essence of Two Hundred Famous Scholars of the National Dynasty, Southern Song Carved Edition, Compiled by Wang Cheng of the Song Dynasty, Not Included in the Siku Quanshu; (7) Xuanhe Bogu Tu, Yuan Carved Edition, Compiled by Wang Fu of the Song Dynasty, Books from the Grand Secretariat Library; (8) Encyclopedia of Literature, Ming Zhengde Movable-Type Printed Edition, Compiled by Ouyang Xun of the Tang Dynasty; (9) Collected Works of Yan Zhenqing, Ming Jiajing Movable-Type Printed Edition, Written by Yan Zhenqing of the Tang Dynasty; (10) Taiping Yulan, Ming Longqing Movable-Type Printed Edition, Compiled by Li Fang et al. of the Song Dynasty; (11) Poems of Meng Haoran, Ming Carved Vermilion and Ink Printed Edition, Written by Meng Haoran of the Tang Dynasty; (12) Collection of Poems by Wang Wei, Ming Carved Vermilion and Ink Printed Edition, Written by Wang Wei of the Tang Dynasty; (13) Ten Bamboo Studio Manual of Painting, Ming Chongzhen Carved, Five-Color Multi-Print Edition; (14) Golden Rules for Encouraging Virtue, Qing Kangxi Carved, Five-Color Multi-Print Edition, Compiled by Emperor Shengzu of the Qing Dynasty; (15) Imperially Commissioned Collection of Ci Tunes, Qing Kangxi Vermilion and Ink Multi-Print Edition, Compiled by Emperor Shengzu of the Qing Dynasty; (16) Ancient Prose Mirror, Qing Kangxi Carved, Five-Color Multi-Print Edition, Compiled by Emperor Shengzu of the Qing Dynasty; (17) Geng Zhi Tu (Illustrations of Agriculture and Sericulture), Qing Kangxi Carved Edition; (18) Tangut Script Golden Light Sutra, Tangut Carved Edition; (19) Tangut Script Sutra and Vinaya Differences, Yuan Carved Edition; (20) Tangut Script Avatamsaka Sutra, Yuan Carved Edition. The above three types were unearthed in Ningxia in recent years.

Wang Zhengting Visited the Exhibition Yesterday

Former Minister of Foreign Affairs Wang Zhengting and his wife visited the exhibition together yesterday morning, browsing for a long time. They expressed deep admiration for the displayed calligraphy, paintings, porcelain, jade, bronze ware, cloisonné, and ancient books. Yesterday, fifty students from the Shanghai Private Academy of Fine Arts also purchased group tickets to visit the exhibition.

Mr. Tang Explained the Reasons for the Fees

Mr. Tang Xifen sent a letter yesterday stating, "Dear Sir, I have been reading the Chinese and English newspapers for the past few days, and many people believe that the price of two dollars for our exhibition ticket is too high. The Preparatory Committee and staff of our exhibition have always held that artistic appreciation should ideally be without cost. However, this preview was not included in the budget, and the exhibition expenses must be covered by ticket revenue. The costs of repairing and renting the venue, display cabinets, security equipment, catalogue printing, specialized work, and the repair and transportation of exhibits, photography, and plate-making are estimated to be no less than 60,000 dollars. Considering the average daily ticket revenue of 1,500 dollars this week, a total of 30,000 dollars will still be lacking in twenty days (the exhibition only lasts twenty days). Furthermore, the printing cost for each Chinese catalogue is 60 cents, while the selling price is only 50 cents (the printing cost for the English catalogue is more expensive, and there are fewer buyers, resulting in even greater losses). As for student visits, they are all given a half-price discount. All of this is something that national museums and art exhibitions cannot do. In other words, our exhibition has made every effort to reduce the expenses of visitors in order to promote the popularization of artistic appreciation, even to the point of incurring losses. Facts speak louder than words. Furthermore, Shanghai is our country's largest metropolis, filled with dust and pollution. Parks are the supreme need for the health of citizens. However, Zhaofeng Park, Hongkou Park, French Park, and all parks charge entrance fees that are exorbitantly expensive. Moreover, the lack of public libraries, museums, art galleries, and children's playgrounds stands in stark contrast to the abundance of corrupting and demoralizing establishments. I have never heard Chinese or foreign individuals in Shanghai voice any objections. This is truly something that I personally find perplexing. I respectfully submit this to your attention and hope you will grant it publication. I wish you all the best in your writing."

Escaped Convict Arrested After Returning to Shanghai: Chen Jinlan, "Snake Skin Jinlan," Hid in Hankou After Escaping But Failed to Make a Living and Returned to Shanghai, Allowing His Capture 122

The murderer Chen Jinlan from Ningbo, nicknamed "Snake Skin Jinlan," 32 years old, was arrested by the French police and prosecuted by the Second Special Court for shooting and killing Chen Zhikui, the owner of the Qianfengtai Incense Shop at 52 Dongxin Bridge Street in the French Concession on April 14, 1933, at approximately 9:00 PM. He was sentenced to fourteen years in prison after trial. The convict appealed, so he was detained in Cell No. 11 of the East Section of the Second Special Court Detention Center (attached to the Second Special Prison on Route Massenet). Subsequently, the Nanjing Supreme Court upheld the verdict after three trials, reducing the sentence to twelve years. During the period leading up to the execution of the sentence, the convict escaped from prison between 3:00 AM and 7:00 AM on December 27th of the previous year. After the discovery, the warden of the detention center transferred the on-duty guards Fang Yuqi and Zhou Wenjin to the Second Court Procuratorate for investigation. He also reported to the Third Branch Procuratorate of the High Court to issue warrants and request that military police, judicial, and other agencies throughout the country work together to apprehend the convict. Warden Gao Xiaoge was also removed from his post and investigated. After the prosecutor concluded the investigation of the two guards, Fang and Zhou, they were deemed to have colluded to facilitate the escape and were prosecuted according to law. The criminal court trial ended recently, sentencing Fang to two years and six months in prison and Zhou to two years in prison. These details have been reported in previous issues. After escaping, Chen fled to Hankou to make a living but failed. A few days ago, he secretly returned to Shanghai. On the 15th, French police detectives Lu Dongliang and Yang Zhongfang discovered that Chen was hiding in the home of his fellow villager Bian Wuchang (27 years old) on the upper floor of a carpenter shop at 32 Laoyong'an Street. They immediately reported to the Western Detective Chief and arrested him quietly at the address at 3:30 PM that afternoon. At the time, Chen attempted to escape by jumping out of the window but was captured by the two detectives. He resisted fiercely, injuring Detective Yang's finger with a bite. The detectives handcuffed him and bound him. The convict then surrendered. Bian Wuchang was also arrested for the crime of harboring a criminal. Both were taken back to the police station for detention and transferred to Criminal Court One of the Second Special Court yesterday. Presiding Judge Wang Gangxu conducted the interrogation (Judge Wang also presided over the first trial of the murder case). According to the police lawyer Gu Shouxi, the police department still needed to investigate the details of Chen Jinlan's escape and requested a postponement for temporary detention pending investigation. The court verified the ages and origins of the defendants and adjourned the hearing to April 26th for further investigation. The defendants were returned to custody. However, in order to understand how the convict was able to escape from a heavily guarded prison, the Chinese and Western detectives, along with Chen, went to the detention center at approximately 3:00 PM yesterday to have him demonstrate the details of his prison escape. It was also heard that in his statement to the police, the convict stated that after escaping, he hid on the Chongming ferry at the Dada Wharf in the South City for one night. At the same time, he sent a letter to his mother in Ningbo to request funds. Because of the high alert, he fled to a small inn on Zhejiang Road, where he borrowed money from friends to go to Hankou. For several months, he was unable to make a living, so he secretly returned to Shanghai. Now that Chen has been apprehended, the two guards, Fang and Zhou, who were imprisoned because of Chen, are appealing the verdict and are expected to have their sentences reduced in the future.

The Shanghai Public Security Bureau submitted the case of Han Debao manufacturing heroin for trial. The judgment was reviewed and approved by the Chairman's Headquarters of the Military Affairs Commission. The prisoner Han Debao was executed by firing squad at the execution grounds after his identity was verified. This is to serve as a warning to others. This announcement is hereby issued for general knowledge. The drivers' strike at the Shanghai Xiang Sheng Bus Company occurred on the 11th of this month. After the suspects were arrested, Zhou Xiangsheng, the general manager of the company, went to the police station and identified Qiu A'gen, Xiao Zishan, Chen Ronglin, Han A'lin, Xu Gengsheng, and Cai A'dong as the leaders of the strike. Detectives He and Fu of the French police discovered on the 13th of this month that the suspects were meeting at the Xiaoyao Hotel at 302 Xinqiao Street and secretly listened from the next room. They saw Qiu A'gen calling the drivers to a meeting and then saw Xiao Zishan whispering to more than ten people near the escalator, demanding that they persist to the end and act against the Xiang Sheng Company in various ways. Detective He could identify Gan Xinchang as one of those present that day. The previous case in which the police prosecuted Yin Xuanqi and Xu Jinsheng for injuring Yang Jinsheng was also because Yin and Xu instructed Yang to join the strike group, but Yang refused and was beaten and seriously injured. Yin and Xu are currently at large. Because the police need to conduct a detailed investigation in this case, they request permission to detain the suspects until next Thursday in accordance with Chapter 6 of the Code of Criminal Procedure. Judge Feng verified the report, questioned the defendants briefly, and approved the detention.

Youth Lacking Ambition: Disappointed in Love, Commits Suicide; Unaware of Life's Meaning, Ashamed Before Society and Nation 128

At the Xingyi Inn, No. 117 Jielu Road, at 6 PM the day before yesterday, a young man arrived, dressed in a Western suit and carrying bedding and luggage. He booked room No. 51, paid the room fee, and registered himself as Guo Cen from Hunan Province, 27 years old, in the guest register. He then went out and did not return to sleep until around 9 PM. Unexpectedly, due to an unknown stimulus, he suddenly had a pessimistic thought and secretly swallowed sleeping pills to commit suicide. The next day at 1 PM, a tea server named Chen Daoqing went to ask if he wanted to extend his stay, but found the door tightly locked. After repeated knocks without response, suspicion arose. He immediately reported to the police, and detective Shen Dehui was dispatched to force open the door. They found Guo moaning on the bed. An ambulance was immediately called to rush him to Tongren Hospital, but the treatment was ineffective, and he died soon after. The detective found two bottles of sleeping pills and a note written in pencil in the deceased's pocket. It read, "Guoying, my dear, my parents are forcing me [to marry someone else]. I have no face to see you anymore. Farewell in the next life," indicating his suicide was likely due to disappointment in love. A menu from the Jingdu Yanbinlou Restaurant on Damalu Road, Xihu New Market, dated April 12th, was also found, suggesting he had come to Shanghai from Hangzhou. The body was transported to the Yuan Corpse Repository on Faelun Road. Yesterday morning, Tang, a prosecutor from the First Special District Court, along with forensic doctor Zhang Yan and clerk Wang Zuji, arrived to examine the body. After hearing the detective's report, Tang ruled that the deceased, Guo Cen, male, had indeed died from poisoning. Since there were no known relatives, the body was handed over to Pushan Villa for burial, and the belongings were confiscated by the police and handed over to the court for public claim.

Huangpu River Dredging Bureau: Scheduled Trial Run of Dredger; Measurement Work at Shentan Completed; Dredging of Tongsha Guan Beginning at the End of the Month 130

The Shanghai Huangpu River Dredging Bureau ordered a world's largest dredger from the German Schichau Shipyard, which arrived in Wusong on the 14th. It is understood that the ship is currently still moored there. A trial run is scheduled for the 24th and 25th of this month. If there are no obstacles, it will be formally delivered. Measurement work at Shentan has also been completed, and dredging can begin at the end of the month. Details are as follows:

Scheduled Trial Run and Delivery: The dredger is named "Jianshe" (Construction) and set sail for China on February 8th. Since arriving in Shanghai on the 14th, it has been moored in Wusong. The Huangpu River Dredging Bureau has scheduled a trial run in the Huangpu River starting on the 24th and 25th. If the results are good, the performance is satisfactory, and there are no other obstacles, it will be formally accepted.

Shentan Measurement Completed: Regarding the dredging of Shentan outside Wusongkou, because the project is enormous, the Hydrographic Department of the Navy assisted with the measurement and other work. The measurement has now been completed. The location of the shoal is southeast of Shentan, in a place called Tongsha Guansha, which is in the center of the Yangtze River estuary, 20 English miles from the Yangtze River mouth and 30 English miles from Wusongkou. After completing the measurement, the Hydrographic Department has now drawn and printed detailed maps for the bureau's reference when the dredging project begins.

Dredging to Begin at the End of the Month: According to Mr. Chadley, Chief Engineer of the Huangpu River Dredging Bureau, the dredging project of the Tongsha Guansha shoal outside Wusongkou will begin at the end of this month and will take approximately one and a half years to complete.

Continued Hearing of the Yong'an Silver Company Case: Ou Jiancheng Surrenders Himself Yesterday; Recounts the Process of Establishing the Company; Ou Released on 30,000 Yuan Bail 131

After the Yong'an Silver Company went bankrupt, the company's directors, general manager, and deputy managers were sued by creditors for fraud and embezzlement in the First Special District Court. After repeated hearings, only Luo Huafang appeared and was released on 5,000 yuan bail. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Zehan continued the hearing. The defendant Ou Jiancheng also surrendered himself along with Luo. However, the remaining defendants Deng Jingfang, Li Du, Mo Dehui, Wang Jiazhen, Lin Kanghou, Wang Yongxin, and others were still unable to be summoned to court. Ou Jiancheng was questioned, and he stated that the Yong'an Silver Company owed more than 230,000 yuan, while 186,000 yuan was owed to the company. If unpaid share subscriptions were included, the two would offset the original surplus. The company's registered capital was one million yuan, with international commodity securities as the main business. The directors of the board were elected by shareholders before September 2nd of last year, with Deng Jingfang as chairman, and Qian Youju and Ye Hancheng as managing directors. The company's founders were himself, Peng Genhui, Qian Youju, Ye Hancheng, and others. In addition to the four founders each subscribing to 5,000 yuan, each was responsible for soliciting shares from other founders. However, Peng Genhui's subscribed 5,000 yuan was never paid. Peng, Qian, and Ye each failed to fully subscribe to 10,000 yuan of the shares they were responsible for soliciting, but he himself solicited 60,000 to 70,000 yuan. For example, Deng Jingfang's initial subscription of 5,000 yuan, and the shares subscribed by Mo Dehui, Wang Jiazhen, Zhang Zilian, Gu Chuntao, and Jiang Qi were all fully paid. However, Lin Qiuhu's subscribed 25,000 yuan was only paid 5,000 yuan. Lin Kanghou himself did not subscribe to shares, but represented 2,500 yuan of equity. The company opened on September 8th of last year. At that time, the subscribed shares totaled more than 300,000 yuan, of which 180,000 yuan was subscribed in Shanghai, but only 104,500 yuan was received. Overseas Chinese in the Philippines subscribed to 150,000 yuan, but none was paid. The reason for the non-payment was that when the company opened, the Social Affairs Bureau discovered that it had not registered with the government and strictly ordered it to be shut down. This news was heard by those who subscribed to shares in the Philippines, who became suspicious of the company and did not pay the subscriptions. Therefore, at the time of opening, the company relied only on the subscriptions received in Shanghai. However, after deducting 20,000 yuan for start-up costs, only more than 80,000 yuan in cash remained. Therefore, at that time, in view of the weak financial resources, the company initially did a small amount of business, intending to wait until the subscriptions were fully collected, obtain registration approval, and then formally open. However, on December 11th, Jiande Bank went bankrupt, and the company's deposits of more than 60,000 yuan were wiped out. Affected by this, the company also suspended business. He previously served as Deputy General Manager of Jiande Bank. After resigning last summer, he initiated the organization of Yong'an Silver Company. However, at that time, if those who had subscribed to shares but not yet paid continued to pay, it would not have followed in Jiande's footsteps. Therefore, after the suspension of business, he went to the Philippines to urge the payment of subscriptions. Unexpectedly, the board of directors suspected that he was evading responsibility and published a warning in the newspaper, causing those who subscribed to shares in Hong Kong and the Philippines to lose trust in him. Although he tried to appeal, it was ultimately futile. Later, Gu Chuntao, at a board meeting, introduced Shen Chengfu's brother, Shen Zufufu, as manager. Shen agreed to subscribe to 40,000 yuan and attract 100,000 yuan in deposits. Deng Zhonghuan also continued to subscribe to 15,000 yuan. He personally advanced more than 3,800 yuan, which was sufficient for application. Unexpectedly, on the day of the resumption of business, Shen not only went back on his word and did not contribute a cent, but on that very day took away a promissory note for 10,000 yuan and 500 yuan in cash and has since avoided him. Luo Huafang and Wang Yongxin were both deputy managers hired by Shen, and so on. Judge Wu verified the statement and concluded that the sum of the two share subscriptions and various deposits, after offsetting the amount owed to others, was short by approximately 100,000 yuan. He then asked how the funds were used, and Ou claimed that they were used for all expenses and losses over several months. The court considered it necessary to verify the account books and the minutes of the board meetings to clarify the contents. It then ordered Ou Jiancheng to pay 30,000 yuan bail and rescheduled the hearing for the afternoon of April 30th.

Construction Plan: According to the person in charge of the association's design section yesterday, the venue construction project is because the conference period coincides with spring and summer, and rain is expected to be frequent. Therefore, all the reed sheds are made of double-layered oiled paper, and gutters and waterways are set up throughout the venue. To the left of the lecture hall is a temporary station for the fire brigade, and to the right is a rest area for police detectives. The office and guest reception area are located on the strip in front of the lecture hall. Three main pedestrian paths, each three meters wide, and four smaller paths, each two and a half meters wide, are opened. A total of 170 spaces are built in the venue. Three memorial archways are built at the main entrance and the three side entrances to enhance the appearance. The project is being overseen by contractor Zheng Liankun, who is working day and night. It is expected that the project will be fully completed by the 20th of this month, and the opening ceremony will be held as scheduled on the 22nd.

Important News from the Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Association: Work Progressing Daily 136

The work of the Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Association, promoted by the Public Works Bureau's Rickshaw Affairs Committee, has been progressing daily in terms of rickshaw pullers' welfare. From January to March of this year, the association's clinic treated 7,037 people, 10,013 attended classes in various educational programs, 25,998 people participated in film screenings and lectures, 463,61 people used the reading room and recreational space, 1,505 rickshaw pullers took baths at the association, 1,156 stayed at the dormitory (about 100 people daily since April), 498 people were provided with relief and nursing care, and the conditions of 16,540 rickshaw pullers were investigated. The association is now planning to establish a free cafeteria (Cafeteria) in the Jiaoyu Road headquarters, where rickshaw pullers can have a meal for a few cents. The association also estimates that about one-third of the rickshaw pullers live in the southern part of the French Concession and Nanshi, and plans to open a branch in that area, which is currently being planned. The association is also studying how to provide insurance, cooperatives, and savings associations for its members to meet their urgent needs. Recently, major cities such as Nanjing, Beijing, and Tianjin have sent letters to the association inquiring about everything for reference.

The Sino-French Savings Society Complies with Orders: Cancels Prize Savings; Will Operate Ordinary Savings in the Future 140

Regarding the ban on prize savings, since the resolution was made at the Second National Financial Conference last year, the Ministry of Finance instructed the competent department to draft specific measures to gradually order the prohibition. Savings societies that voluntarily change to ordinary savings should submit their own replacement measures to the Ministry for review and approval. Otherwise, the collection of new accounts will be suspended, and the existing accounts will be continued by the Trust Bureau of the Central Bank until the savings period expires. It is understood that the Sino-French Savings Society has now formulated replacement measures and will operate ordinary savings. Those who have previously joined the prize savings of the society will be transferred to special savings accounts from the date of cessation of prize draws. For those who originally deposited 15 yuan, 3 yuan and 7.5 cents will be deducted each month. For those who originally deposited 12 yuan, 3 yuan will be deducted each month, and so on by analogy. The repayment period will be shortened from 15 years to 14 years. An application has been submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval. In addition, the Universal Savings Society is also reportedly planning replacement measures to comply with the laws and regulations of the Ministry of Finance.

The Shou Chang Steamer Returns to Shanghai and Suspends Service; Cargo Handlers and Stewards Dispersed; Old Stewards Complain to the Company That New Crew Members Can Only Return to Yichang 141

The Sanbei Company's Shou Chang Steamer, on this trip to Yichang, had its eighteen cargo handlers and stewards, dispatched by the local Seamen's Association on the grounds that the ship's port of registry was Yichang, disembark, forcibly occupy the passenger cabins, and expel the original crew's stewards. Now that the Shou Chang has returned to Shanghai, the Sanbei Company does not recognize these cargo handlers and stewards and has ordered them to return to Yichang immediately. The solutions are detailed below:

Stewards' Complaints

The twenty-four original Sichuan stewards of the Shou Chang, upon the ship's arrival in port yesterday, went as a group to the company to report to Manager Chu Keqing that the eighteen cargo handlers and stewards forcibly dispatched by the Yichang Seamen's Association on this return trip from Yichang to Shanghai, upon boarding the ship, immediately occupied seventeen passenger cabins, preventing the ship's stewards from attending to passengers. In Yichang, they even dragged the head steward to the union, forcibly compelling him to recognize the new personnel and dismiss the original stewards. The clothes and luggage of the original stewards were taken away indiscriminately by these people. They requested the company to make a decision.

Shou Chang Service Suspended

The Shou Chang, after arriving in Shanghai and unloading the goods transported from the upper Yangtze River, immediately suspended service and entered the shipyard for repairs. All shipboard officers were reassigned to the Fuyang Steamer. The stewards decided to temporarily disband to avoid providing the Yichang Seamen's Association-dispatched cargo handlers with a pretext for further action.

Stewards Return to Yichang

The eighteen cargo handlers and stewards dispatched by the Yichang Seamen's Association, after arriving in Shanghai with the ship, were unable to remain on board due to the need for the ship to enter the dock. Yesterday, they all left the ship and went ashore, temporarily staying in small inns in the 16th Puli area. Lacking funds, they found it difficult to stay for long and reportedly plan to return to Yichang by boarding the Fuyang when it goes upriver.

Liu Wenqing's Adopted Daughters Misbehave; Lawsuit Filed to Terminate Adoption; Youdong Withdraws Part of Termination Request; Youlin Files Countersuit Seeking Living Expenses 142

Liu Wenqing, a Fujian native who formerly held a position in the Ministry of the Navy, retired and came to Shanghai after the Fujian Incident, living as a recluse at No. 3 Rongfuli, Zhangjia Garden, Maitehesi Road, West Shanghai. On March 9th of this year, around 9:00 AM, Liu's twenty-two-year-old adopted daughter, Liu Youlin, and nineteen-year-old adopted daughter, Liu Youdong, suddenly disappeared simultaneously. Liu Wenqing reported this to the police and engaged a lawyer to publish a notice in the newspaper, declaring the termination of the adoption relationship with both Youlin and Youdong. He also filed a petition with the Civil Division of the First Special Court, requesting a ruling to approve the termination of the adoption. Later, Liu Wenqing discovered that Liu Youdong had been seduced and hidden by Chen Zhenghong, a Yangzhou native who operated an auto repair shop across the street. He reported this to the police, who, on March 26th, ordered detectives to arrest Chen Zhenghong and Liu Youdong. Liu Youlin was also found at the Donghai Inn in Yuegui Lane, Wuma Road. The next morning, they were escorted to the First Special Court. The police, according to Article 257 of the Criminal Law, prosecuted Chen for enticing Liu Youdong, a woman under twenty, to leave her guardian, and for engaging in sexual relations. The trial resulted in Chen being sentenced to one year of imprisonment. Considering it was his first offense, Liu Youdong was ordered to be taken back by her adoptive father, Liu Wenqing. However, Liu Youlin, because her adoptive father refused to continue the adoption, wandered homeless and also engaged a lawyer to criminally accuse her adoptive father, Liu Wenqing, in the First Special Court of instigating murder and other crimes. After receiving the indictment, the court ruled that Liu Youlin and Liu Wenqing were relatives and, according to the law, could not sue each other. Therefore, the court rejected Liu Youlin's suit. Yesterday morning at 9:00 AM, Judge Mo Runhua presided over the Fourth Civil Court to try Liu Wenqing's case requesting the termination of the adoption of Liu Youlin and Liu Youdong. Liu Wenqing was absent and sent lawyers Dong Yu and Yao Junyu to represent him in court and present the case, requesting approval for the termination of the adoption. Subsequently, Liu Youdong testified that she still lived with her adoptive father, had now repented, and was willing to abide by family rules and had obtained her adoptive father's understanding. Judge Mo then turned to Liu Wenqing's representative lawyer to inquire about his opinion, who stated that Liu Youdong's will was weak and she had not thoroughly awakened. On the 6th of this month, she had received a phone call from Chen Zhenghong and left alone, although she returned shortly thereafter, but she was still secretly communicating with Chen, with lingering attachments, and there was fear of future changes. He requested that she be ordered to clearly express that if there were any more improper behaviors in the future, the adoption should be unconditionally terminated. Upon hearing this, Liu Youdong immediately stated that she had repeatedly considered this matter and was determined to repent. The plaintiff's representative lawyer then requested that the termination of the adoption of Liu Youdong be withdrawn, while the termination of the adoption of Liu Youlin should still proceed. Liu's mother was purchased as a maid by the plaintiff's mother when she was over ten years old. Later, because the plaintiff had no daughters and saw that she was of good quality, she was adopted as an adopted mother. Unexpectedly, after adulthood, her temperament changed drastically, and she often went out on her own. Moreover, this time Youdong's relationship with Chen Zhenghong was also introduced by Youlin. Therefore, the plaintiff, in order to maintain his reputation and family rules, requested the termination of the adoption. Liu Youlin then filed a counterclaim against Liu Wenqing, arguing that Youlin was a weak woman with no ability to support herself. If the adoption were terminated, she would have no means of living and would have to study in order to find a way out in the future. Therefore, she demanded that Liu Wenqing pay her a lump sum of 36,000 yuan for living and educational expenses. After the lawyers for both sides debated, Judge Mo announced that the judgment would be announced on Saturday morning of this week.

Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau Implements Plant Pest and Disease Inspection Starting on the 20th of This Month 147

Plant pest and disease inspection originated in Germany, followed by France, Austria, the United States, Sweden, and Belgium. Our country has not yet implemented it. As a result, pests and diseases such as the red bollworm and corn smut are imported along with overseas plants, spreading widely and causing increasing damage. The losses suffered by Chinese farmers are incalculable. As for exported plants, there is no legal agency to inspect and certify them, and farmers are unaware of prevention and control measures, resulting in those with attached insects and bacteria being either completely destroyed by the importing country or ordered to be shipped back. In severe cases, imports are even prohibited, which reduces foreign trade. On the other hand, pests attached to foreign goods are imported in a steady stream, without anyone stopping them. Our country has almost become a dumping ground for the world's inferior plants, which is truly deplorable. Therefore, the implementation of plant pest and disease inspection in our country is urgently needed in terms of business needs. The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry entrusted experts to begin preparations in October of the 21st year of the Republic of China. Due to various factors such as investigation and design funding, personnel, and contact with various countries in the East and West, everything has only recently been finalized. The detailed inspection rules have now been submitted to the Executive Yuan for record and are scheduled to be implemented starting on the 20th of this month. The Bureau has sent these detailed rules to the Jianghai Customs to request its review and assistance, and has also sent them to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to forward them to relevant merchants.

Wu and His Son Go Abroad to Investigate the Development of Agriculture and Eradication of Leprosy in Hainan Island, and Give a Talk to Reporters 148

Qiongya, a remote island county, is the largest island in our country, with fertile land and abundant mineral resources. According to our country's statistics, the annual import of rubber, coffee, coconut oil, etc., exceeds 100,000 yuan. Moreover, the businesses of overseas Chinese are becoming increasingly difficult. If they can return to their homeland and start actively developing the island, it would be a way to seek an economic outlet for the nation and reclaim our rights and interests. It is believed that foreign industrialists in our country will agree with this idea. Now, Wu Xianshou, an agricultural expert from Hainan, plans to go abroad to investigate the actual conditions of industries in various places for in-depth research, so that he can learn from them. Mr. Wu arrived in Shanghai yesterday and is scheduled to take the Deliya north during the day, first to Qingdao and Dalian, and then to East Po, Japan, according to Mr. Wu.

Investigate Agriculture: Qiongya is the only tropical region in our country, with fertile land, a mild climate, and abundant mineral resources. Recently, the local area has become peaceful. If we can engage in mining and planting as much as possible, such as rubber, coffee, cinchona, coconut, and sugarcane, the future is full of unlimited hope. Although my brother and I previously studied agriculture at Lingnan Agricultural College in Guangzhou and the Agricultural College of the Philippines, after returning to China, we engaged in self-operated farms, planting and raising livestock. The results of four years of experimentation have been very satisfactory and gratifying. Now, for the sake of learning from others, we are going to Japan, Taiwan, and other places to investigate local planting, animal husbandry, agricultural product manufacturing, water and electricity, etc. Japan has many situations similar to China, so we are going there to learn from them.

Study Leprosy: Accompanying Mr. Wu on this trip is his father, Wu Weifan, the owner of Guanghui Drugstore in Haikou, Qiongzhou. He has been working hard to help leprosy in Qiongya and is the founder of the Qiongya Leprosarium. He told the interviewer yesterday that in the 21st year of the Republic of China, my brothers invited various Chinese and Western circles in Qiongya to organize a leprosarium construction committee. With donations of 20,000 yuan from local people, the Shanghai China Leprosy Relief Association, and philanthropist Hu Wenhu, we built eight dormitories and one treatment center. Recently, the Guangdong Provincial Government allocated 6,000 yuan, and we are now accommodating more than 100 male and female lunatics. My brothers are going north this time to report on the situation to the Shanghai China Leprosy Relief Association and go to Japan, Taiwan, and other places to investigate leprosy relief and treatment methods to learn from them.

Separate Introduction Letters: It is reported that Mr. Wu and his son once went to Guangdong to meet with Pacification Director Chen Jitang and personally sent a letter to Mr. Kawasai Tatsuo, the Japanese Consul-General in Guangzhou. Mr. Kawasai then wrote letters to the Kobe Maritime Police Department and the Governor-General of Taiwan, requesting them to provide proper hospitality at that time to facilitate the investigation. The Hong Kong Chinese General Chamber of Commerce also sent separate letters to the Chinese Embassy in Japan, the Taiwan Chinese Chamber of Commerce, etc.

Free Talk

Random Musings on "Romanticism" 159

— Junchong

When discussing Romanticism in art, we must be aware that, just as Realism in art does not necessarily align with Materialism in philosophy, Romanticism in art is not the same as Idealism in art. In fact, certain Romantic art (such as the fantastical Romantic literature of German Idealism in the early 19th century) embodies an Idealist approach, but at the same time, the facts of art history also show that Romantic works characterized not by a delusional reflection of objective reality, but by an emphasis on the "possibilities" and "driving forces of development" contained within reality itself (such as Shelley and Heine's lyrical poetry) belong to Idealist Romantic art. In art history, it has always been a declining class, due to its historical mission. When it has lost its progressiveness and begins to move towards its own grave, it dares not face reality, and thus indulges in the grand longing for past achievements and the fascination with ruins, emitting an anti-historical evolutionary art trend. In this kind of Romantic art, it is not, as Mr. Xin Ren said, "because it is itself a part of darkness, so even though their 'utopia' takes on various forms, in essence, it is an ode to blackness." It also contains this kind of "utopia" -- a feeling that there is a need to cleanse this darkness, but they do not objectively observe reality, see the driving force of history, and entrust their realistic utopia to it, but instead start from their own subjective ideas and subjectively fantasize about the artistic expression of objective reality.

In evaluating progressive Romanticism, it is necessary to first pay attention to its historical development and the changes in its historical essence. The Romanticism of the rising stage of a new class and the Romanticism of the construction stage of the highest society after grasping political power are somewhat different in nature. What can be said to be the characteristic of early Romanticism is an ardent, great, sublime ideal of realizable possibilities that stimulates the artist's emotions in real life, an "emotional" emphasis and expression. It is precisely because of this "emotional emphasis" that what is embodied in the early Romanticism of the rising class is often a more abstract, sublime ideal of longing, a eulogy for the birth of a bright future with a terrible heat. This "emotional emphasis" is precisely the characteristic of early Neo-Romanticism. Of course, this characteristic also varies due to the individual writer's qualities, talents, and technical proficiency.

The Neo-Romanticism currently being advocated is, to some extent, different from early Neo-Romanticism. Currently, Neo-Romanticism is being treated as one element of Realism, as a colorful, abundant, and unrestrained creative method. The reason why current Neo-Romanticism is different from early Neo-Romanticism is because the romance that is the object of Romanticism is no longer just something "possible" existing in reality itself, but has become an element of objective reality. Romance not only exists in the present and will be realized in the future as something "possible," but already exists in reality. It is precisely because this element of romance is inherent in objective reality that Romanticism is being explained as an element of Realism. Therefore, at this time, "emotional emphasis" is no longer the only characteristic of Romanticism. At this time, Romanticism has become inseparable from Realism and has been integrated and synthesized into Realism. Because, from the standpoint of "reflection theory," if Realism at this time is to see through and express the social and human reality, then it must inevitably be the reason for Romanticism.

On this point, I agree with Mr. Xin Ren's saying: "Any emerging literature in history is necessarily 'realistic and romantic.'" However, I will only add a little restriction here: "Realistic and romantic" is the characteristic of emerging literature in history, but it is necessary here to see through its historical development and the essential changes that come with that development, and we cannot be satisfied with "realistic and romantic" as a characteristic of the literature of every emerging class in history. At the same time, we should also pay attention to its "realistic" historical class limitations. Only by explaining this point can we fully understand the essential difference between Burr's Realism and Neo-Realism. Especially in the former point (i.e., the historical development of the Romanticism of the emerging class and the essential changes that come with this development) must be given deep attention. I think that Mr. Xin Ren's view of the Romanticism of the emerging class as a kind of "utopia" that is a "passionate 'longing' for light through dark reality" is only the initial form of the Romanticism of the new class, not the entire posture of its entire development. Without understanding this point, without understanding the historical development and qualitative changes of Neo-Romanticism, it is impossible to understand the current Neo-Romanticism.

In the Murky Current 160

— Wang Ying

Unwilling to talk about the pain of life, everyone likes to see smiling faces - even if that smile is very strenuous - I understand the so-called "survival" of more of this reason, therefore, how many times, I picked up the pen, and finally could not write a decent thing.

Living in a gloomy mood, tears can flow endlessly into the heart like a river; in the cold and lonely late night, facing the lightless lamp, crying out loud, but, in the crowd, you have to laugh pleasantly, even so, you still can't live a little better; you have to drag out a meager existence in the midst of falls and slanders, in the midst of bullying and blows. The whole era is in suffering, so, how are the young people living in this era being tormented to the point of being unable to breathe.

In Tokyo, I saw a new Russian film, titled "Survival," I remember very clearly, I ran for two days, bought four tickets, and finally bought a seatless admission ticket. It was winter, and the theater did not have heating or other facilities, but, it was steamed with the crowd of people, sweating, the film was only a play with three people, and it was the passing things in two hours, using the sound of the clock walking, to seize the emotions of the audience; the general idea is this: everyone, - to put it more broadly, every living thing - needs to yearn for "survival," but, today's world has these two kinds of people, one kind is only concerned with their own survival, and does not care about the survival and death of others, and even deprives others of the right to survive; one kind hopes that everyone lives. However, we are unfortunately surviving in the control of the society of these kinds of people who "only care about their own survival."

It seems that I have not lived a good day since I was pushed into this crowd of people with bloody mouths. This world has no distinction between "black and white" or "right and wrong," and what you touch every second is only gray and hazy, and it is a gloomy, never-ending black night with heavy fog. What surrounds us here is boundless cold and melancholy. Facing this endless night, I am already occasionally moaning without being able to make a sound.

Qingdao's Park 161

— Liu Ming

Let the surprisingly large sandy road lead us into the German locust forest. Unnamed little birds are happily chirping where they cannot be seen. On the trees that have not yet sprouted leaves, there are large bird nests, and magpies with white bellies and black feathers quietly fall to the ground, pecking at something, and then quietly fly up again. Occasionally, two horses pull a clumsy cart loaded with stones, and walk out with a jerk in the shouts of rough men, but after a while, they return to silence again. If you walk to a higher place and look out from the branches, the pine-covered hillside and the green sea surface are all around not far away, appearing as if they are exhausted.

Who would think of it as visiting a park like this? It's simply like taking a long trip in the mountains and forests.

Qingdao's First Park is really lovely. It covers an area of about 1,600 acres, with many roads in the middle, which can be used for cars. Each road is named after a flower, such as Ginkgo Road, Begonia Road, Plum Blossom Road, and Cherry Blossom Road. The day we went was when the cherry blossoms were in full bloom. It had rained last night, and the roads were slightly damp, so the strolling tourists were lucky enough not to eat the dust swept up by the cars, as they used to.

Spring in the north is very late. The peach blossoms and elm leaf plum blossoms still have a timid and cold look, half revealing their red faces. The only ones that compete with the exotic cherry blossoms are the golden bell flowers of goose yellow and the blood-like azaleas. Imagining the south of the Yangtze River at this time, isn't it the "late spring in March" when "various flowers grow on trees and groups of orioles fly around"? But there are still people who deliberately run from the south to this place to see the spring scenery for two or three days and then return in a hurry. In the eyes of those who live in the north, it is a bit silly. However, it is still smarter to spend the money that could be used to relieve disaster victims in this way.

Probably because of the morning, there are few modern men and women in the park. Most of those who walk slowly under the cherry blossom trees are ordinary businessmen and rough men from the countryside. From this point, Qingdao Park's ability to share happiness with everyone, unlike Shanghai Park, which requires money to play, is worthy of praise.

Here, we also saw old women stamping their small feet, which were once praised by guests at the time of their marriage, messily on the sandy road covered with petals. Perhaps people do not feel deeply painful about this yet. Some young girls are also hobbling with a pair of unnatural feet, tracing the footsteps of their grandmothers. This is not very common in the park, but it is quite common in the places where ordinary people live. According to Ye Gongchuo's "Qingqiu Travel Fragments," "The municipal government actively persuades people to unbind their feet, declaring that after a certain period of time, people will be sent to sun and test whether it has been implemented, and female staff will be sent to check. There are even those who hanged themselves for fear of the test, and those whose fathers and brothers who did not unbind their feet by the deadline were detained and fined ten yuan, and they vented their anger on the women after returning, forcing them to commit suicide. Therefore, the municipal government can only proceed slowly." The simplicity of the northerners is respectable, but the degree of stubbornness is frightening.

On the way back, we picked up two peach branches with buds on the side of the seaside park (probably discarded by the villagers after being scolded by the police), inserted them in a bottle, and let spring be with us for some time.

Mr. Juqing (15) 162

— Ke Ling

Before he even got home, a student came running in a panic to tell him: The teacher from the school had already caught a private tutor at his house. – An even bigger surprise attack!

Hearing the news, as quickly as lightning, Mr. Juqing's iron-green complexion turned deathly pale. He stopped, without saying a word. In an extremely short period of time, two questions agitated in his mind: Go back? Not go back?

His whole body was as scorched as if on fire. After a long while, he finally walked towards his house.

There were three young teachers in the room, one thin and tall, and one small with eyebrows and eyes turned upside down, individually rummaging through the students' desks and drawers, searching for ancient books such as "Primer of Juvenile Studies" and "Mencius" to clip under their arms: still the old method of investigating private tutors. More than a dozen students stared at them with wide eyes. Principal Zhang was wearing a dark blue serge student uniform, and inserting both hands into his trouser pockets, a posture that added a bit of arrogance to his demeanor. Mr. Juqing ran in, and he was stretching out one foot in front, as if at "ease," not knowing what he was interrogating Mrs. Juqing about.

When Mr. Juqing stepped into the study, everyone was stunned for a moment. A momentary silence in the tense air.

The person who came in was panting breathlessly, and it took him a long time to catch his breath. Forcibly calming himself, he squeezed out a trace of a bitter smile, cupping his hands and saying:

"Please sit, please sit, gentlemen."

Facing the old man's humble demeanor, Principal Zhang felt that it was not necessary to be polite at all. He straightened his chest, as if his body had grown a lot.

"I won't sit." His head nodded slightly downward (others couldn't see it at all), considering it a nod: "We are here to investigate."

"Yes, yes." Mr. Juqing tried his best to appear amiable, "We will slowly improve everything."

The weak sunlight near dusk shone softly on the corner of the wall, and the study already looked dusky. In the short time of silence, Mr. Juqing used the greatest patience to calm himself, anxiously thinking about how to peacefully deal with the current situation; but Principal Zhang was feeling slightly perplexed by Mr. Juqing's overly humble attitude. There was a surge of unstable fire in his heart, looking for an opportunity to erupt.

Notes on the Exhibition of Chinese Art at the International Exhibition 163

— Cao Juren

Exhibiting ancient Chinese art to gentlemen, ladies, young masters and young mistresses, is originally like playing the lute to a cow. In the two hours I spent at the exhibition, I heard several young mistresses lamenting: "Really nothing to see! Really nothing to see!" Two dollars is originally nothing to them; but they always feel that it is more reasonable to spend these two dollars to see Mei Lanfang's opera or to watch dancing, dog racing, etc. Their opinions are of the following types:

"The portraits are painted very realistically!"

"So, these are truly Tang Bohu and Zhu Zhishan's paintings!"

"This person is indeed very famous!"

"Was Emperor Taizu of Song the same as Emperor Hongwu?"

"Emperor Taizu of Song was Zhao Kuangyin."

"Zhao Kuangyin on the stage has a red face, why is this person's face not red at all?"

"What's the point of these broken copper and scrap iron dug out of the mud?" (Referring to the bronzes unearthed from Xinzheng)

In addition, there are connoisseurs who are half-baked scholars, and they also have various opinions:

"Qianlong and Yongzheng were truly talented emperors. Look, there are 'Treasures viewed by the Emperor' on them."

"This poem is well written."

"Zhao Mengfu's (they pronounce it Tao) calligraphy is nothing special, but it has a talent's air."

"This is a true Song edition of Mr. Wu Liu's biography." (Copied down with a fountain pen)

"This is called oracle bone, used for divination." (Referring to a piece of cattle bone.)

"This is called and that is called a cauldron. What's the point?"

"Jade is still more beautiful than bronze."

These are generally the kinds of discussions made by the three or four hundred noble viewers; I seemed to hear the artworks sighing. This is truly not an exhibition of ancient Chinese art, but rather an exhibition of the foolishness, baseness, and ignorance of some city residents who are tired of eating fish and meat. This is the inevitable result of the two-dollar ticket price: those who truly appreciate art and truly want to understand ancient culture are all kept outside the door, unable to come in and take a look!

Looking at all the exhibits at the exhibition, the calligraphy and painting section has inevitably taken up too much space. There are indeed very good pieces in the calligraphy and painting; but it is too much to introduce works on paper as Chinese art. Europeans have already seen Chinese murals, woodcuts, and various other things. Why only introduce works on paper? Chinese collectors and connoisseurs in the past had very poor aesthetic knowledge; many of the so-called precious works were actually just tricks colluding with each other among collectors and connoisseurs, and had very little real value. Treasures viewed by the Emperor are even less reliable; whatever Qianlong appreciated, many ministers followed suit in praising; but what he appreciated was often the worst, partly due to his incompetence, and partly due to his despotism. Collectors all have a common problem: whatever they collect is the best in the world; although many works have been commented on by many collectors, they are still highly untrustworthy. Collectors rarely have a historical perspective; they do not understand the path of Chinese art development. If the arrangement and classification are not appropriate, it will make the viewer unable to grasp any concept. The chaotic arrangement of the calligraphy and painting section is enough to prove the aesthetic ability of the connoisseurs.

The arrangement of the exhibits in each room, with the archaeological items selected by the Academia Sinica as an example, is the most refined and organized, and is obviously the work of archaeological experts. The arrangement of the bronzes section is also very appropriate, and the textual research work is done very meticulously; this is enough to show the progress in the study of artifacts in the past thirty years. The ancient book section does not specialize in Song and Yuan editions, but lists various engraved editions and fine transcriptions. This is the best way to explain the cultural aspects; we must admire the vision of the person who arranged it. Naturally, the best-arranged is what the Shanghai citizens ignore the most; however, I do not believe that after arriving in London, the British academic community will reverse the original values like the Shanghai compradors; the bronze section at least should give Western archaeologists some new stimulation!

Education News

The City's Literacy Education Committee Has Formulated Enrollment Methods for Literacy Schools and Methods for Investigating Out-of-School Citizens. Investigation and Awakening Committees Are Established in Each District. 164

The municipal government has decided to implement compulsory literacy education from July 1st of this year. All situations have been recorded in this newspaper. The Literacy Education Committee is now actively preparing. The enrollment methods for literacy schools and the investigation methods for out-of-school citizens have been formulated. The following is an excerpt:

Enrollment Methods for Literacy Schools

(1) The city will implement compulsory literacy education from July 1, 1935. All out-of-school citizens in the city should receive literacy education. (2) The city's compulsory literacy education will be implemented for a temporary period of one year, from July 1, 1935 to June 30, 1936. (3) The class time of literacy schools shall be selected by each out-of-school citizen within the prescribed time during the investigation, from three to six times. The literacy schools shall coordinate and designate the time. Domestic servants and employees of stores shall be provided with convenience for classes by their employers and shall not be deliberately obstructed. (4) Citizens who are required to receive literacy education shall, if they delay enrolling in school without reason after receiving the enrollment notice from the literacy school, be fined from 20 cents to 5 yuan in addition to being forced to enroll, or be ordered to perform labor service for more than one hour and less than five days. The same shall apply to those who are absent from class without reason. Those who ask for leave midway due to a reason and are approved by the literacy school shall make up for the class within the specified time. For the aforementioned punishments, adult men and women shall be fined themselves, and minors shall be fined their parents. (5) The punishments in Article 4 shall be reported by each literacy school to the district office for decision and then notified to the Public Security Bureau for execution. They shall be reported to the city's Literacy Education Committee on a monthly basis for record. (6) Literacy schools shall not charge students any fees, and textbooks shall also be provided by the school. However, other school supplies such as pencils and paper shall be provided by the students themselves. (7) Students of literacy schools who pass the examination at the end of the education period shall be issued an initial general education certificate by the Literacy Education Committee. (8) Citizens who are required to receive literacy education shall, if they are unable to attend school due to an accident, report the reason to the office or the nearby literacy school, which shall then report it to the district office. If the district office verifies that it is true, they may be allowed to make up for the class outside the school on their own. The methods for off-campus tutoring shall be formulated separately. (9) These methods shall be approved by the Shanghai Municipal Government and submitted to the Ministry of Education for record before being announced and implemented.

Methods for Investigating Out-of-School Citizens

(1) In order to understand the situation of out-of-school citizens in the city and to implement literacy education, the committee has specially established investigation committees in each district to assist district offices in handling the investigation of out-of-school citizens. (2) The investigation committee in each district shall be organized by the director of the district office, who shall select a number of personnel from the following institutions in the jurisdiction and request the city's Literacy Education Committee to appoint them, and report to the municipal government for record: (1) Principals of public and private schools, (2) Directors of public and private social education institutions, (3) Chiefs of Public Security Bureau stations, (4) Committee members of the party headquarters, (5) Municipal committee members, (6) Those who are enthusiastic about public welfare and have a good reputation, (7) Commanders or captains of the security regiment, (8) Staff of the investigation section of the district office. The chairman of the investigation committee shall be appointed by the city's Literacy Education Committee. (3) The committee shall appoint the members of each investigation committee at the same time and transfer them to their original positions, requesting their respective competent authorities to order them to cooperate in the handling of the matter. (4) The tasks of the investigation committee are as follows: (1) Investigate out-of-school citizens aged 13 to 50 living in the district, regardless of their native or guest籍 (the out-of-school children under the age of 13 have already been investigated in 1934), (2) Investigate the addresses of schools, private schools, and social education institutions in the district, and temples, guilds, or other public places that can be used to set up literacy schools, (3) Assign teachers and staff of schools, senior grades of primary schools, and students of secondary and above schools, staff of social education institutions, police chiefs of public security bureaus, party members of district branches, local security personnel, and other personnel who can perform investigation work as investigators, (4) Allocate investigation areas according to the streets, roads, villages, and houses in the district, (5) Determine the investigation time according to the assigned investigation area, (6) Guide the investigators in the investigation and form-filling methods, (7) Supervise the investigators to conduct investigations in batches according to the district city and time period, (8) Conduct selective spot checks in each investigation area during the investigation process, (9) Collect the investigation forms and bind them into volumes according to streets, roads, villages, and houses, (10) Other matters related to the investigation.

Methods and Schedule for Awakening

(5) After the district office has selected the investigators and assigned the investigation areas, it shall report to the city's Literacy Education Committee immediately. (6) The areas connected to each district shall be contacted and allocated by the joint district investigation committee, and the connections shall be made in earnest to avoid omissions or duplication. (7) The investigators shall fill in the forms in accordance with the investigation instructions, stating the status of the out-of-school citizens, and the handwriting must be clear and easy to recognize. According to a certain street, road, village, or house, indicate the number of members on the form and send it to the investigation committee in order. (8) Investigators who are primary school students in senior grades may form groups of two or three people to cooperate with other investigators. (9) During the investigation period, the investigators shall shorten the completion time of their original duties as much as possible and set aside time to start the investigation. (10) The investigation form paper shall be printed and distributed by the city's Literacy Education Committee. (11) The work schedule of the investigation committee and the investigators is as follows: May 5th, the investigation committee shall complete the preparation work for items 3, 4, 5, and 6 of Article 4 of these methods and all other preparations that should be made. May 8th, the investigators shall begin the investigation. May 31st, the investigators shall complete the investigation. June 2nd, the investigation committee shall organize and bind the investigation form volumes. June 4th, the investigation shall be completed and all form volumes shall be sent to the district office. (12) The members of the investigation committee and the investigators are all voluntary positions, but according to the size of the area, each district shall be given 50 to 100 yuan for transportation and meals. (13) These methods shall be implemented after being approved by the city's Literacy Education Committee and reported to the municipal government for record.
